Act No. 254/2001 Coll.
Act on Waters and on Amendments to Certain Acts (the Water Act)
https://www.zakonyprolidi.cz/cs/2001-254

Amount: 98/2001
Valid from: 25.07.2001
Effective from: 01.01.2002

Current version 01.02.2022 - 22.12.2023

254
ACT
of 28 June 2001
on waters and on amendments to certain acts (the Water Act)

The Parliament of the Czech Republic has adopted the following Act:

PART ONE
ACT ON WATERS (THE WATER ACT)

TITLE I
INTRODUCTORY PROVISIONS

§ 1
Purpose and Subject of the Act

(1) The purpose of this Act is to protect surface and groundwaters as endangered and irreplaceable components of the environment and natural resources, to lay down the conditions for the sustainable use of water resources, for the conservation of water resources and the prevention of water scarcity, and for the preservation and improvement of the quality of surface and groundwaters, to create conditions for reducing the adverse effects of floods and droughts, and to ensure the safety of waterworks in accordance with the law of the European Communities¹). The purpose of this Act is also to contribute to ensuring the supply of drinking water to the population and to the protection of aquatic ecosystems and terrestrial ecosystems directly dependent on them.

(2) This Act regulates legal relations concerning surface and groundwaters, the relations of natural and legal persons to the use of surface and groundwaters, as well as relations to land and structures with which the occurrence of these waters is directly connected, in the interest of ensuring the sustainable use of these waters, the safety of waterworks, and protection against the effects of floods and droughts. Within the framework of the relations regulated by this Act, the principle of cost recovery for water management services, including the costs of related environmental protection and the costs of the resources used, is taken into account, in accordance with the principle that the polluter pays.

§ 2
Definition of Terms

(1) Surface waters are waters naturally occurring on the earth's surface; they do not lose this character if they flow through temporarily covered sections, natural cavities under the earth's surface, or in overground conduits.

(2) Groundwaters are waters naturally occurring below the earth's surface in the saturated zone in direct contact with rocks; waters flowing through underground drainage systems and waters in wells are also considered groundwaters.

(3) A water body is a defined, significant concentration of surface or groundwater in a specific environment, characterized by a common form of occurrence or common properties of the water and features of the hydrological regime. Water bodies are divided into surface water bodies and groundwater bodies.

(4) A surface water body is a defined concentration of surface water in a specific environment, for example in a lake, in a reservoir, or in the bed of a watercourse.

(5) A heavily modified water body is a surface water body that has been substantially altered in character as a result of human activity.

(6) An artificial water body is a surface water body created by human activity.

(7) A groundwater body is a defined concentration of groundwater in the relevant aquifer or aquifers; an aquifer is understood as a rock layer or formation of rock layers with sufficient permeability to allow for significant continuous accumulation of groundwater or its flow or abstraction.

(8) A water resource is surface or groundwater that is used or can be used to meet human needs, particularly for drinking purposes.

(9) Management of surface or groundwaters is their impoundment by means of waterworks, the use of their energy potential, their use for navigation or timber rafting, for fish or waterfowl farming, their abstraction, the discharge of wastewater into them, and other ways in which their properties can be utilized or their quantity, flow, occurrence, or quality can be influenced.

(10) A river basin is an area of land from which all surface runoff flows through a network of watercourses and, where applicable, lakes to the sea at a single river mouth, estuary, or delta.

(11) A sub-basin is an area of land from which all surface runoff flows through a network of watercourses and, where applicable, lakes to a certain point of a watercourse (usually a lake or a confluence of rivers).

(12) A hydrogeological district is an area with similar hydrogeological conditions, type of aquifer, and groundwater circulation.

(13) A water line is a continuously connected network of watercourses and other water lines, including parts impounded by a waterwork and temporarily covered sections, interrupted only at places where natural infiltration occurs.

(14) Other water line is a flowing surface or groundwater that does not correspond to the definition of a watercourse under § 43.

(15) An authorized person is a professionally competent legal person authorized by a decision of the Ministry of Agriculture to carry out technical safety supervision over waterworks, including the preparation of a technical safety supervision program and the preparation of the scope of technical safety supervision measurements, within the scope of its authorization, and to prepare expert opinions for the classification of waterworks into categories from the perspective of technical safety supervision.

(16) An authorization is a decision of the Ministry of Agriculture granting authorization to carry out technical safety supervision over waterworks, including the preparation of a technical safety supervision program and the preparation of the scope of technical safety supervision measurements, and to prepare expert opinions for the classification of waterworks into categories from the perspective of technical safety supervision.

§ 2a

(1) The status of surface waters means a general expression of the status of a surface water body determined by its ecological or chemical status, whichever is worse.

(2) The status of groundwaters means a general expression of the status of a groundwater body determined by its quantitative or chemical status, whichever is worse.

(3) Ecological status is an expression of the quality of the structure and functioning of aquatic ecosystems associated with surface waters.

(4) Good status of surface waters means such a status of a surface water body where both its ecological and chemical status are at least good.

(5) Good status of groundwaters means such a status of a groundwater body where both its quantitative and chemical status are at least good.

(6) Good chemical status of surface waters means the chemical status necessary to achieve the objectives of water protection as a component of the environment (§ 23a), where the concentrations of pollutants do not exceed environmental quality standards.

(7) Good chemical status of groundwaters means the chemical status necessary to achieve the objectives of water protection as a component of the environment (§ 23a), where the concentrations of pollutants do not exceed environmental quality standards.

(8) An environmental quality standard means the concentration of a pollutant or group of pollutants in water, sediment, or living organisms which must not be exceeded for reasons of protecting human health and the environment.

(9) The quantitative status of groundwaters is an expression of the degree to which a groundwater body is affected by direct and indirect abstractions.

§ 3
Rights to Waters and the Legal Nature of Water

(1) Surface and groundwaters are not subject to ownership and are not part of or appurtenant to the land on which or under which they occur; rights to these waters are regulated by this Act.

(2) Waters that have been abstracted from surface and groundwaters are not considered surface and groundwaters.

(3) In case of doubt as to whether it is or is not surface or groundwater, the water authority shall decide.

§ 4

(1) This Act applies to waters that are reserved minerals under a special act¹a), and to natural medicinal sources and sources of natural mineral water for which a certificate has been issued under a special act,²) only where expressly provided.

(2) For the purposes of this Act, mine waters are considered surface or groundwater, and this Act applies to them, unless a special act¹a) provides otherwise.

TITLE II
MANAGEMENT OF WATERS

Division 1
Basic Obligations

§ 5

(1) Anyone who manages surface or groundwaters is obliged to ensure their protection and to ensure their economical and purposeful use under the conditions of this Act, and further to ensure that their energy potential is not degraded and that other public interests protected by special legal regulations³) are not violated.

(2) Anyone who manages surface or groundwaters for production purposes is obliged, in order to fulfill the obligations under paragraph 1, to implement effective measures in production leading to the economical use of water resources and taking into account the best available technologies.

(3) When carrying out construction⁴), its alterations, or changes in its use, the builder is obliged, according to the character and purpose of the use of these structures, to ensure water supply and wastewater disposal by a designated sewer system. If a sewer system is not available at the location, wastewater shall be treated by direct purification with subsequent discharge into surface or groundwaters. In case of technical infeasibility of the methods according to the first and second sentences, wastewater may be accumulated in a sealed tank (cesspool)⁴) with subsequent transport of the accumulated water to a facility approved for its treatment. Furthermore, the builder is obliged to ensure the reduction of runoff of surface waters originating from atmospheric precipitation on these structures (hereinafter "stormwater") by accumulation and subsequent use, or by infiltration on the property, evaporation, or, if none of these methods of reducing stormwater runoff is possible or sufficient, by its retention and controlled discharge or a combination of these methods. Without fulfilling these conditions, the construction, alteration of the construction before its completion, use of the construction, nor a decision on the subsequent permitting of the construction or a decision on the change in the use of the construction may be permitted.

§ 5a

Water authorities, as the authorities concerned, shall, in their opinions on proposals for land-use planning documentation, take into account the objectives of protecting surface and groundwaters, their economical use, and the creation of conditions for reducing the adverse effects of floods and droughts in built-up and developable areas. Water authorities shall provide land-use planning bodies with data and documents for demarcating areas suitable for reducing and retaining stormwater runoff and for implementing water features.

Division 2
Management of Surface Waters

§ 6
General Management of Surface Waters

(1) Anyone may, at their own risk, without a permit or consent from the water authority, abstract surface waters or otherwise manage them for their own needs, provided no special technical equipment is required.

(2) A permit or consent from the water authority is also not required for the collection of surface waters by simple means on individual plots and structures or for changing the natural runoff of water for the purpose of protecting them from the harmful effects of these waters.

(3) The general management of surface waters must not endanger the quality or health safety of the water, disturb the natural environment, worsen runoff conditions, damage banks, waterworks and equipment, fish farming equipment, or violate the rights and legally protected interests of others.

(4) The water authority may, by a decision or a measure of a general nature, without compensation, regulate, restrict, or prohibit the general management of surface waters if required by public interest, especially if it leads to a violation of the obligations under paragraph 3 or for reasons of personal safety. The competence of other administrative authorities to set conditions for the use of these waters for bathing⁵) is not affected by this Act.

§ 7
Use of Surface Waters for Navigation

(1) The use of surface waters for navigation and the abstraction of water necessary for the operation of vessels do not require a permit from the water authority.

(2) Operators of vessels are obliged to equip them with the necessary equipment for the accumulation of wastewater and to operate it properly, if wastewater may arise during their use or operation, and are obliged to prevent the leakage of wastewater and harmful substances from vessels into surface waters.

(3) Operators of ports, special service facilities⁵⁶), and special vessels⁶) designated for the transport of fuel and waste from vessels (hereinafter "service vessel") are obliged to ensure the supply of vessels with propellants and operating fluids and the removal of wastewater or harmful substances from vessels in ports or by means of special service facilities.

(4) The transfer of wastewater or harmful substances from vessels and the supply of vessels with propellants or operating fluids outside of ports is prohibited if their volume in individual cases exceeds 50 liters or if these activities are not ensured by a special service facility or service vessel.

(5) On surface waters in the protection zones of water resources of the I. degree and on reservoirs designated by a permit or decision of the water authority under § 8 para. 1 let. a) point 4 or under previous regulations for fish farming, the navigation of vessels with combustion engines is prohibited. If it is not a waterway of transport importance,⁷) this navigation is prohibited on water reservoirs and watercourses determined by the Ministry of Transport in agreement with the Ministry of the Environment in cooperation with the Ministry of Agriculture by a decree. Surface waters may be used for navigation only in such a way that it does not endanger the interests of recreation, water quality and aquatic ecosystems, the safety of persons and waterworks; the scope and conditions of the use of surface waters for navigation are determined by the Ministry of Transport in agreement with the Ministry of the Environment in cooperation with the Ministry of Agriculture by a decree.

(6) The navigation prohibition under paragraph 5 does not apply to vessels of the State Navigation Administration, the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic, the armed forces of the Czech Republic, the Police of the Czech Republic, the municipal police, the customs administration of the Czech Republic, and the administrators of watercourses, if they are used for official purposes, furthermore to vessels used in connection with the construction, maintenance, or operation of waterworks or other structures on watercourses or on adjacent lands, vessels of persons performing duties under this Act, or vessels used for the necessary provision of health services or for flood protection. The navigation prohibition under paragraph 5, with the exception of the protection zones of water resources of the I. degree, does not apply to vessels of persons who have a valid permit for the management of waters under § 8 para. 1 let. a) point 4 or under previous regulations, for the purpose of managing reservoirs designated by such a decision for fish farming.

(7) The water authority, after consultation with the State Navigation Administration, decides on exemptions from the prohibition and restriction under paragraph 5 in individual cases.

(8) The Police of the Czech Republic and the State Navigation Administration shall supervise compliance with the prohibition of navigation of vessels with combustion engines on surface waters under paragraph 5, as well as the use of surface waters for navigation with regard to the established scope and conditions of their use.

Division 3
Permit, Consent, and Opinion

Section 1
Permit

§ 8
Permit for the Management of Surface or Groundwaters

(1) A permit for the management of surface or groundwaters (hereinafter "permit for the management of waters") is required

a) for surface waters, unless it is a case of general management of them

for their abstraction,

for their impoundment, or possibly accumulation,

for the utilization of their energy potential,

for the use of these waters for fish or waterfowl farming, or possibly other aquatic animals, for business purposes,

for other management of them,
b) for groundwaters

for their abstraction,

for their accumulation,

for their pumping for the purpose of lowering their level,

for the artificial enrichment of groundwater resources with surface water,

for other management of them,
c) for the discharge of wastewater into surface or groundwaters,
d) for the pumping of surface or groundwaters and their subsequent discharge into these waters for the purpose of obtaining thermal energy,
e) for the pumping of contaminated groundwaters for the purpose of reducing their contamination and for their subsequent discharge, unless it is an activity carried out on the basis of a permit under the act on mining activities, explosives, and the state mining administration⁷b),
f) for the use of mine water as a substitute source under a special act¹a).

(2) A permit for the management of waters is issued to natural or legal persons upon their application. A natural or legal person who has a valid permit for the management of waters under paragraph 1 or under previous regulations (hereinafter "the entitled person") is authorized to manage waters to the extent and for the purpose for the period specified in the valid permit.

(3) A permit for the management of waters is not required
a) for pumping tests during hydrogeological surveys or during surveys of the yield of groundwater sources, if they last less than 14 days and the water abstraction during this period does not exceed 1 l/s,
b) for the abstraction of surface and groundwaters for determining and assessing the status of these waters (§ 21),
c) for a one-time abstraction of surface or groundwaters in cases of rescue work during extraordinary events, fires, and other natural disasters,
d) for the management of surface waters during exercises and interventions of the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic and fire protection units, the Police of the Czech Republic, the municipal police, or the armed forces of the Czech Republic; this management must be discussed in advance with the water authority during exercises,
e) for the utilization of the energy potential of groundwaters, if no abstraction or pumping of groundwater occurs,
f) for the use of mine waters by organizations during mining activities for their own needs or for the discharge of mine waters by organizations¹a),
g) for the discharge of wastewater from relief chambers into surface waters.

(4) In case of doubt as to whether it is a management of surface or groundwaters and what type of management of surface or groundwaters it is, the water authority shall decide.

§ 9

(1) A permit for the management of waters is issued for a limited period of time. The permit for the management of waters shall specify the purpose, scope, obligations, and, where applicable, the conditions under which this permit is issued. The basis for issuing a permit for the management of groundwaters is the opinion of a person with professional competence, unless the water authority decides otherwise in exceptional cases.⁸)

(2) A permit for the discharge of wastewater cannot be issued for a period longer than 10 years; in the case of discharging wastewater with particularly hazardous substances or hazardous substances according to Annex No. 1, for a period longer than 4 years.

(3) If the water authority permits the abstraction of surface or groundwaters subject to charges (Title XI Division 1 and Title XII) for a period longer than 1 year, it shall also determine the amount of the permitted annual abstraction.

(4) The abstraction of groundwater for the purpose of producing bottled infant or spring water may be permitted if the groundwater source meets the quality requirements for bottled infant or spring water according to the decree regulating the requirements for the quality and health safety of bottled water and the manner of its treatment⁸a); if the groundwater can be treated according to this decree, the limits for its quality are considered met in the indicators in which it can be treated.

(5) A permit for the management of waters that can only be carried out by using a waterwork can be issued only simultaneously with the building permit for such a waterwork in a joint proceeding, unless it is a waterwork that already exists or has been permitted, or which will be permitted in a joint land-use and building proceeding under a special act⁴) by an administrative authority other than the water authority. In the case of issuing a permit for the management of waters simultaneously with the permit for the construction of a waterwork, the operative parts of these permits are mutually conditional; if both of these decisions are challenged by appeal, the appeal proceeding on the appeal against the permit for the management of waters shall be conducted first, while the appeal proceeding, the subject of which is the building permit for the construction of a waterwork, is suspended until the day the decision of the appellate administrative authority issued in the proceeding on the appeal against the permit for the management of waters becomes final.

(6) A permit for the management of waters for the utilization of their energy potential cannot be issued for a period shorter than 30 years. The water authority, following the procedure under § 12 para. 2, shall extend the validity of the permit by the period specified in the existing permit, unless the entitled person has been finally imposed an administrative penalty for repeated violation of obligations established by or under this Act.

(7) A permit for the management of waters for their impoundment, or possibly accumulation, is issued for the duration of the use of the waterwork that enables such management of waters.

(8) When permitting the management of waters for the purpose of fish or waterfowl farming, or possibly other aquatic animals [§ 8 para. 1 let. a) points 4 and 5], the water authority shall specify in the permit the conditions for the use of harmful substances for feeding fish in cases other than those specified in § 39 para. 12 and for the treatment of surface waters in reservoirs intended for fish farming. If the permit specifies conditions for the use of hazardous and particularly hazardous harmful substances, this permit may not be issued for a period longer than 4 years. The provisions of § 39 para. 1 second sentence do not apply to the entitled person who handles harmful substances within the scope of the conditions according to the first sentence.

(9) A permit for the management of waters for the artificial enrichment of groundwater resources with surface water may be issued only if the use of the surface or groundwater source for this purpose will not endanger the objectives set under § 23a for this water source or the objectives set under § 23a for the artificially enriched groundwater source.

(10) A permit for the management of waters issued as a basis for a joint land-use and building proceeding under a special act⁴) loses its validity if the joint permit, by which the construction is located and permitted under the special act⁴), does not become final within 3 years from the day it became final.

§ 10

(1) The following are obliged to measure the quantity of water they manage and to transmit the results of this measurement to the relevant river basin administrator according to the procedure under § 22 para. 2:
a) the entitled person who has a permit for the management of waters under § 8 para. 1 let. a) point 1 or § 8 para. 1 let. b) point 1 in a total quantity of at least 1000 m³ of water in a calendar year or 100 m³ of water in a calendar month,
b) the entitled person who has a permit for the management of waters under § 8 para. 1 let. a) point 5, § 8 para. 1 let. b) points 2 to 5, or § 8 para. 1 let. d), e), or f) in a total quantity of at least 6000 m³ of water in a calendar year or 500 m³ of water in a calendar month,
c) anyone who has a permit for the management of waters in a quantity of at least 6000 m³ of water in a calendar year or 500 m³ of water in a calendar month, which are a natural medicinal source or a source of natural mineral water or which are a reserved mineral.

(2) The entitled person who has a permit for the impoundment, or possibly accumulation, of surface waters and if the permitted volume of water impounded by a waterwork in a watercourse or water accumulated by a waterwork exceeds 1,000,000 m³, is obliged to measure the quantity of impounded or accumulated water and to transmit data about it to the relevant river basin administrator according to the procedure under § 22 para. 2.

(3) The method and frequency of measuring the quantity of water under paragraph 1 for individual types of water management, and measuring the quantity of accumulated or impounded water under paragraph 2 shall be determined by the Ministry of Agriculture after consultation with the Ministry of the Environment and the Ministry of Health by a decree.

(4) The water authority may specify further details of these measurements in the permit for the management of waters. In an extraordinary situation, the water authority may, at the proposal of the entitled person, determine the method and scope of measurement outside the proceeding for a permit for the management of waters, for a limited, strictly necessary period.

§ 11

(1) The rights and obligations arising from a permit for the management of waters, which was issued for a purpose associated with ownership of land or structures, shall pass to their acquirers, provided that these lands or structures will continue to serve the purpose stated in the permit. This also applies to their users for the period of use of these lands or structures to the extent corresponding to the scope of the user's rights to them, arising from the mutual relationship between the owner and this user. The acquirers of these lands or structures, or their users, are obliged to notify the water authority that the transfer or transition of the land or structure with which the permit for the management of waters is associated has occurred, within 2 months from the day of their transfer or transition, or the creation of rights to their use.

(2) A permit for the management of waters does not create rights to foreign lands and structures, nor does it create a legal obligation for the water authority, the watercourse administrator, or the owner of the waterwork to compensate the entitled person for the inability to manage waters in the maximum permitted quantity and with certain properties.

(3) Unless the water authority determines otherwise, the entitled person may allow another to exercise their permit for the management of waters.

(4) If the permitted management of waters is necessary in the public interest and the entitled person does not use their permit at all or only partially, the water authority may impose on them the obligation to allow the use of their waterwork or facility for the permitted management of waters by another natural or legal person designated by the water authority, for a strictly necessary period or until a decision on its expropriation or restriction of ownership rights, for reasonable compensation.

§ 12
Amendment and Revocation of a Permit for the Management of Waters

(1) The water authority may, ex officio, amend or revoke a permit for the management of waters if
a) the entitled person does not use the issued permit for the management of waters or uses it only minimally without a serious reason for a period longer than 2 years; this does not apply in the case of a permit under § 8 para. 1 let. b) point 1 for the abstraction of water from backup sources for the supply of drinking water from a public water supply,
b) the entitled person, who has a permit for the discharge of wastewater into surface or groundwaters, was obliged to connect to a sewer system under a special legal regulation⁸b),
c) when determining the minimum level of groundwater, if it has not yet been determined, or upon its change.

(2) The water authority may amend or revoke a permit for the management of waters at the request of the entitled person. If the permit was issued to another person, the applicant must prove that they are the entitled person from this permit.

(3) The water authority shall amend or revoke a permit for the management of waters, also in a proceeding under paragraph 1 or 2, if it is necessary
a) to achieve the water protection objectives adopted in the river basin plan (§ 24 and 26),

b) to fulfill the programs for reducing the pollution of surface waters (§ 34 para. 2 and § 35 para. 1),
c) to fulfill the program for reducing the pollution of surface and groundwaters by hazardous harmful substances and particularly hazardous harmful substances (§ 39 para. 3),
d) for the supply of drinking water according to the water supply and sewerage development plan⁸c).

(4) If the entitled person applies for a change in the validity period of the permit for the management of waters, the permit shall not expire until the application has been finally decided; the application must be submitted before the expiry of the validity period of the permit for the management of waters.

(5) The provisions of § 9 to 11 shall apply mutatis mutandis to the amendment and revocation of a permit for the management of waters.

§ 13
Expiry of a Permit for the Management of Waters

A permit for the management of waters expires
a) upon the expiry of the period for which it was granted,
b) upon the demise of the waterwork (§ 55) enabling the permitted management of waters, unless the water authority sets a deadline and conditions for restoring the structure to its original state within 1 year of the demise of the work, in which case the permit expires upon the fruitless expiry of this deadline,
c) upon the demise of the legal person or the death of the natural person to whom the permit was granted, unless the entitlement has passed to another acquirer under § 11 para. 1.

§ 14
Permit for Certain Activities

(1) A permit for certain activities is required
a) for planting trees or shrubs in floodplains to an extent that affects runoff conditions,
b) for the extraction of sand, gravel, mud, with the exception of mud for medicinal purposes, pebbles, etc. (hereinafter "river material") from lands on which a watercourse bed is located,
c) for geological works involving intervention into land in floodplains (§ 66) and in protection zones of water resources,
d) for the backfilling of abandoned arms of watercourses,
e) for returning a watercourse to its original bed (§ 45),
f) for the disposal of mining waste into surface waters¹⁰b).

(2) A permit for the activities listed in paragraph 1 let. a) or b) is not required if they are carried out by the watercourse administrator (§ 48) in connection with its administration or by the owner of a waterwork in connection with the maintenance of a water reservoir. Furthermore, it is not required under paragraph 1 let. a) if carried out by a forest owner for reasons of forest regeneration and in activities imposed by Act No. 289/1995 Coll., on forests and on the amendment and supplementation of certain acts (the Forest Act), as amended.

(3) If it follows from the nature of the matter, the water authority may specify in the permit conditions and the period for which the permit is granted.

§ 15
Building Permit for Waterworks

(1) The construction of waterworks, their alterations, and changes in their use, as well as their demolition and removal, require a permit from the water authority. A permit for the construction or alteration of a waterwork that is to serve for the management of waters permitted under § 8 may be issued only if the corresponding management of waters is permitted or if the management of waters is permitted simultaneously with the permit for the construction or alteration of the waterwork (§ 9 para. 5). In the case under § 126 para. 5, the permit for the construction or alteration of the waterwork is not issued simultaneously with the decision under the Act on integrated prevention; the rights and obligations arising from the permit for the construction, alteration of the waterwork, or change in its use may be exercised no earlier than the date on which the decision under the Act on integrated prevention becomes final.

(2) A building permit or notification is not required for structural modifications of water mains and sewer systems, provided their route is not changed.

(3) The water authority shall specify in the building permit the obligations, and where applicable, the conditions under which it is issued, and the purpose which the waterwork is to serve. The water authority may, in the building permit, impose an obligation to submit the operating rules of the waterwork no later than with the application for the issuance of a final use permit.

(4) Together with the application for the issuance of a final use permit for the construction of water mains, waterworks facilities, water treatment plants, sewer mains including sewer facilities, or wastewater treatment plants, which are part of water mains or sewer systems for public use⁵³), the applicant shall submit a permit for their operation⁵⁴).

(5) The water authority exercises the powers of a special building authority under a special act.¹⁰)

(6) A waterwork may be permitted in a joint land-use and building proceeding under a special act⁴), unless this act provides otherwise.

(7) The water authority may invite the applicant for a building permit to submit a draft of the manipulation rules, or possibly a calculation of the special flood wave, for waterworks impounding or accumulating surface waters and structures utilizing their energy potential.

(8) When permitting waterworks, their alterations, changes in their use, and their removal, the possibility of overcoming the work by transfer or navigation in places of use of surface waters for recreational navigation must be taken into account, and the protection of aquatic and water-dependent ecosystems must be considered. These waterworks must not create barriers to the movement of fish and aquatic animals in both directions of the watercourse, and their passage within the waterway must be enabled. This does not apply in cases of
a) ponds or water reservoirs for fish farming or structures for torrent and gully control,
b) if required by flood protection or another public interest, or
c) when overcoming the work or the movement of fish and aquatic animals in both directions of the watercourse cannot be ensured due to technical infeasibility or disproportionate costs.

(9) If a permit issued under § 8 para. 1 or under previous regulations on the management of waters expires, the water authority shall decide on the conditions for the further existence, or possibly removal, of the waterwork that enabled the management of waters.

(10) The water authority may order the cessation of work on a structure or the removal of a structure constructed or being constructed under an extraordinary procedure according to the Building Act by order of the flood authority of the municipality, the municipality with extended powers, or the region. The issuance of this decision is the first act in the proceeding.

(11) Waterworks are not eligible for assessment by an authorized inspector; this does not apply in the case of the construction of water mains, sewer mains, and sewer facilities that do not require a permit for the management of waters.

(12) The water authority shall notify the relevant building authority of a decision to demolish a waterwork.

§ 15a
Notification of Waterworks and Water Management Modifications

(1) For the construction of waterworks intended for the treatment of wastewater up to a capacity of 50 population equivalents, the essential components of which are CE-marked products under a special legal regulation¹⁰c), a notification to the water authority is sufficient. The provisions of the Building Act on the notification of constructions shall apply mutatis mutandis to their notification.

(2) The notification of a waterwork under paragraph 1 shall contain
a) the particulars according to the Building Act⁴),
b) the category of the CE-marked product,
c) project documentation prepared by a person who has obtained authorization for this activity under a special legal regulation¹⁰d),
d) the method of wastewater discharge,
e) the opinion of the relevant watercourse administrator in the case of discharging wastewater from the waterwork into surface waters,
f) the opinion of the river basin administrator,
g) the opinion of a person with professional competence in the case of discharging wastewater from the waterwork through soil layers into groundwaters, and
h) the operating rules.

(3) For the construction of a waterwork up to an area of 20,000 m² with a dam height of up to 2.5 m, which serves for the impoundment and accumulation of water and is not subject to technical safety supervision or meets the criteria for classification into category IV of technical safety supervision, a notification to the water authority is sufficient. The provisions of the Building Act on the notification of constructions shall apply mutatis mutandis to the notification of a waterwork under the first sentence.

(4) The notification of a waterwork under paragraph 3 shall contain
a) the particulars according to the Building Act⁴) and further a binding opinion of the land-use planning authority under § 96b of the Building Act, whereby a land-use decision or land-use consent is not issued; unless it is a project carried out in an area protected under part three or four of the Act on Nature and Landscape Protection, a binding opinion of the nature protection authority is not required,
b) project documentation prepared by a person who has obtained authorization for this activity under a special legal regulation¹⁰d), which contains an introductory report, a summary technical report, site plans, documentation of structures and technical and technological equipment, a documentary part, a proposal for a plan of construction inspection checks, a proposal for the classification of the waterwork into a category of technical safety supervision and the scope, or possibly conditions, for carrying out technical safety supervision (§ 61 para. 6), data on the maximum impounded and accumulated water level, normal impounded and accumulated water level, and data on the volume of impounded and accumulated water at the normal level,
c) an expert opinion for the classification of the waterwork into a category with a proposal of conditions for carrying out technical safety supervision (§ 61 para. 6),
d) the opinion of the river basin administrator,
e) the opinion of the relevant watercourse administrator, if the waterwork or the management of waters affects a watercourse,
f) the opinion of the municipality in whose territorial district the water conditions may be affected.

(5) If the waterwork or the management of waters affects a watercourse, the project documentation under paragraph 4 let. b) shall also include data on water flows in the watercourse and a proposal for the minimum residual flow, including the place and method of its measurement (§ 36 para. 2).

(6) The owner of a waterwork is obliged to notify the water authority of maintenance works that could negatively affect the environment or the stability of the waterwork. The notification is also subject to the restoration of waterworks destroyed by a natural disaster or accident and water management modifications; earthworks and terrain modifications in the natural beds of watercourses and on adjacent lands, which do not substantially change the natural beds of watercourses, do not require a building permit or notification. In the cases under the first and second sentences, the deadline for the water authority to state that it has no objections is 15 days; within this period, the building authority may prohibit the notified restoration or maintenance works or water management modifications.

(7) If the water authority consents to the construction of a notified waterwork under paragraph 1, the management of waters under § 8 para. 1 let. c) is also considered permitted; the provision of § 9 para. 2 does not apply in such a case.

(8) If the water authority consents to the construction of a notified waterwork under paragraph 3, the management of waters under § 8 para. 1 let. a) point 2 is also considered permitted, and, where applicable, the management of surface waters for the purpose of filling this waterwork and returning surface water back to the watercourse or surface waters is considered permitted. With the consent of the water authority to the notification, the permit for the management of waters mentioned in the first sentence is valid for the duration of the use of the waterwork.

(9) Consent to the construction of a notified waterwork under paragraph 1 or 3 is also delivered to the river basin administrator and, if the waterwork or the management of waters affects a watercourse, to the watercourse administrator. This does not affect the delivery of the consent to the construction of the notified building project under the Building Act.

§ 15b
Notification of Land Modifications

(1) For the implementation of land modifications serving to retain water in the landscape up to a depth of 1.5 m with an area of more than 300 m² but not more than 20,000 m² in an undeveloped area, which do not have a common boundary with a public land communication, a notification to the water authority is sufficient. The provisions of the Building Act on the notification of constructions shall apply mutatis mutandis to the notification of land modifications under the first sentence.

(2) The notification of land modifications under paragraph 1 shall contain the particulars according to the Building Act⁴) and further a binding opinion of the land-use planning authority under § 96b of the Building Act, whereby a land-use decision or land-use consent is not issued. Unless it is a land modification carried out in an area protected under part three or four of the Act on Nature and Landscape Protection, a binding opinion of the nature protection authority is not required.

(3) The documentation of land modifications under paragraph 1 shall contain
a) an introductory report with basic data on the land modifications,
b) data on the expected effects of the land modifications on the surroundings, a technical description of the procedure and method of work, data on backfill materials, on the place and method of depositing excavated materials, on the method of their compaction and surface treatment,
c) a site plan on a copy of the cadastral map, and
d) a site plan on a scale of usually 1:500 with the proposed land modifications marked, the lands on which their effects will be manifested, including the marking of established protection or safety zones or floodplains, and the necessary geometric parameters determining the positional and height placement of the land modifications in the site plan.

§ 15c
Removal of Waterworks for the Purpose of Restoring the Natural Beds of Minor Watercourses

(1) For the removal of a waterwork by which the bed of a minor watercourse, constructed before 2002, is regulated, altered, or established, which no longer fulfills its function or fulfills it only partially or has lost its purpose, and which is located on land outside a built-up area or developable area, a notification by its owner to the water authority is sufficient for the purpose of restoring the natural bed of the minor watercourse. The provisions of the Building Act on the removal of constructions shall apply mutatis mutandis to the notification.

(2) The removal of a waterwork on the basis of a notification under paragraph 1 must not lead to a significant deterioration of the functions of the minor watercourse or to a significant impact on the rights and legitimate interests of the owners of the lands forming its bed or adjacent to it.

(3) The notification of the removal of a waterwork under paragraph 1 shall contain:
a) the particulars according to the Building Act⁴),
b) the consent of the relevant watercourse administrator; this does not apply if the watercourse administrator is the owner of the waterwork.

(4) If the water authority consents to the notified removal of a waterwork under paragraph 1, the bed of the minor watercourse at its location is considered the natural bed of the minor watercourse.

(5) If the notification does not have the prescribed particulars or suffers from other defects, the water authority shall invite the owner of the waterwork to remedy the deficiencies in the submission, provide a reasonable deadline for this, and instruct them on the consequences of not remedying the deficiencies within this deadline. If the water authority concludes that the notification is incomplete or the conditions for issuing consent are not met, it shall decide by a resolution to conduct a water management proceeding for the permission of the removal of the waterwork under § 15; this resolution is notified only to the owner of the waterwork and cannot be appealed. The water management proceeding is initiated by the final force of the resolution.

§ 16
Permit for the Discharge of Wastewater Containing a Particularly Hazardous Substance or a Priority Hazardous Substance into a Sewer System

(1) The discharge of wastewater which may reasonably be expected to contain one or more particularly hazardous substances or priority hazardous substances into a sewer system requires a permit from the water authority.

(2) If wastewater containing particularly hazardous substances or priority hazardous substances is discharged into the sewer system from one or more technologically defined production units, a permit under paragraph 1 is required separately for each of these production units. If industrial wastewater containing particularly hazardous substances or priority hazardous substances is discharged into a sewer system that is part of a production site, and is treated in a facility intended for the treatment or disposal of this wastewater, the water authority may issue a permit up to the point of discharge of the wastewater from this facility.

(3) When issuing this permit, § 38 paras. 10 to 12 shall apply mutatis mutandis.

(4) The water authority shall, in the permit under paragraph 1, impose an obligation to establish a control point and a method for measuring the volume of discharged wastewater, the degree of its contamination with particularly hazardous substances or priority hazardous substances, and the manner in which the measurement results will be submitted. It shall take into account the requirements of the approved sewer regulations.

(5) If a facility with sufficient efficiency is installed for the removal of particularly hazardous substances or priority hazardous substances from wastewater discharged into a sewer system, the water authority may, in the permit, specify conditions for the operation of such a facility instead of the obligations under paragraph 4.

Section 2
Consent

§ 17

(1) The consent of the water authority is required for constructions, facilities, or activities for which a permit under this Act is not required, but which may affect water conditions, namely
a) for constructions and facilities on lands on which the beds of watercourses are located, or on lands adjacent to such lands, if these constructions and facilities affect water conditions,
b) for the establishment of long-distance pipelines and structures enabling the underground storage of substances in terrestrial cavities, as well as for storage facilities, landfills, or possibly reservoirs, if the operation of these structures and landfills may significantly endanger the quality of surface or groundwaters,
c) for constructions, mineral extraction, or land modifications in floodplains; the provision of § 67 is not affected by this,
d) for constructions at a distance of up to 15 m from the air side of the toe of a protective dike of a watercourse,
e) for constructions in protection zones of water resources,
f) for disposal sites for the management of mining waste or for a decision on the obligation to collect and treat contaminated water and leachate under another legal regulation¹⁰b),
g) for wells for utilizing the energy potential of groundwaters, from which groundwater is not abstracted or pumped; unless this Act provides otherwise, the water authority may, in the proceeding for granting this consent, require the applicant to submit an opinion of a person with professional competence⁸),
h) for the storage of carbon dioxide in natural rock structures under another legal regulation⁴⁹), or
i) for geological works associated with an intervention into land, the purpose of which is the subsequent use of the exploratory work as a construction for the collection of groundwater or for wells for utilizing the energy potential of groundwater.

(2) For an application for consent to wells under paragraph 1 let. g) or geological works under paragraph 1 let. i) in a protection zone established under the Spa Act, the applicant shall submit an opinion of a person with professional competence under the Act on Geological Works⁸).

(3) If it follows from the nature of the matter, the water authority may specify in the consent conditions and the period for which the consent is granted.

(4) Consent is binding for the competent authorities in proceedings under special acts⁴), ⁷b), ¹⁰b) in the cases listed in paragraph 1.

(5) Consent under paragraph 1 is not required for activities which are necessary during exercises or interventions of the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic and fire protection units, the Mine Rescue Service, the Police of the Czech Republic, the municipal police, and the armed forces of the Czech Republic, which in cases of exercises proceed in agreement with the relevant water authority.

(6) Before issuing consent under paragraph 1, the water authority shall assess the possibility of deteriorating the status or ecological potential of a surface water body or the status of a groundwater body. At the same time, it shall assess whether the implementation of the project will not lead to such a change in physical conditions that would prevent the achievement of good status or good ecological potential of the surface water body or good status of the groundwater body. If it concludes that the implementation of the project may lead to a deterioration of the status or ecological potential of the surface water body or a deterioration of the status of the groundwater body or prevent the achievement of good status or good ecological potential of the surface water body or good status of the groundwater body, it shall inform the applicant that without an exemption under § 23a para. 8 it is not possible to permit or carry out the project and that without this exemption, consent under paragraph 1 cannot be issued.

Section 3
Opinion

§ 18

(1) Anyone who intends to locate, construct, change, or remove a structure or facility or carry out other activities, if such a project may affect water conditions, energy potential, quality, or quantity of surface or groundwaters, has the right, after sufficient documentation of the project, to receive an opinion from the water authority as to whether this project is possible from the perspective of the interests protected under this Act, and, where applicable, under what conditions.

(2) The water authority shall also issue an opinion on the use of sources of natural mineral water certified under a special act.²)

(3) An opinion is not a decision in an administrative proceeding and does not replace a permit or consent of the water authority issued under this Act.

Division 4
Water Management Records

§ 19

(1) Administrative authorities and bodies of local self-government are obliged to keep records of the decisions, measures of a general nature, binding opinions, consents issued by them, and notifications submitted to them to which they gave consent under this Act, and also parts of decisions which, under the Act on integrated prevention, replaced decisions issued under this Act.

(2) The Ministry of Agriculture, in cooperation with the Ministry of the Environment, shall by a decree determine the scope and manner of keeping the records under paragraph 1, define the scope of data and the manner of their entry into the public administration information system¹¹), and the manner of transferring information from the existing water management records and summary water management records¹²) into this information system.

(3) Administrative authorities and bodies of local self-government are obliged to enter the decisions, measures of a general nature, binding opinions, and identification data issued by them from the records they keep under paragraph 1 into the public administration information system (§ 22 paras. 3 and 4) to the extent specified by the decree issued under paragraph 2 and to transmit them in electronic form to the Ministry of Agriculture no later than the 15th day of the first month of the following quarter.

(4) River basin administrators are obliged to continuously enter selected data from final decisions, measures of a general nature, and binding opinions of water authorities into the public administration information system to the extent specified by the decree issued under paragraph 2.

§ 20
Data Entered in the Real Estate Cadastre

(1) Dams, dikes, weirs, structures established for navigation purposes in the beds of watercourses or on their banks, structures for the use of water energy, and tailings ponds, if they are connected to the ground by a solid foundation, are recorded in the Real Estate Cadastre.¹²a) Details of the definition of these waterworks shall be determined by the Ministry of Agriculture in agreement with the Czech Office for Surveying, Mapping and Cadastre by a decree.

(2) Protection zones of waterworks (§ 58 para. 3) under paragraph 1 and protection zones of water resources (§ 30) are marked in the Real Estate Cadastre with data on the method of property protection.¹³)

(3) The water authority is obliged to send the relevant cadastral office the data necessary for the registration of the protection of the area under paragraph 2 within 30 days from the day the decision by which this area protection was defined became final.

TITLE III
STATUS OF SURFACE AND GROUNDWATERS

§ 21

(1) The assessment and evaluation of the status of surface and groundwaters serve to provide a basis for the performance of public administration under this Act, for water planning, and for providing information to the public, and is carried out according to the river basins of surface waters and the hydrogeological districts of groundwaters.

(2) The assessment and evaluation of the status of surface and groundwaters includes in particular
a) assessing the quantity and quality of surface and groundwaters, including their impact by human activity, and assessing the status of water bodies and the ecological potential of heavily modified and artificial water bodies,
b) maintaining a water balance (§ 22 para. 1),
c) establishing, maintaining, and updating records of

water lines and objects on them, hydrological river basins, hydrogeological districts, and water reservoirs,

water bodies, including heavily modified and artificial water bodies,

the quantity and quality of surface and groundwaters, the status of water bodies, and the ecological potential of heavily modified and artificial water bodies,

abstractions of surface and groundwaters, discharges of wastewater and mine water, and the accumulation of surface waters in water reservoirs,

international river basin districts in the territory of the Czech Republic and sub-basins (§ 24),

protected areas of natural water accumulation (§ 28),

protection zones of water resources (§ 30),

sources of surface and groundwaters that are used or are expected to be used as sources of drinking water,

sensitive areas (§ 32),

vulnerable areas (§ 33),

areas of surface waters used for bathing (§ 34),

surface waters that are or are intended to become permanently suitable for the life and reproduction of native species of fish and other aquatic animals (§ 35),

main drainage and main irrigation facilities (§ 56),

floodplains (§ 66).
The scope and method of processing, storing, and transmitting the data included in the records, including statistical and cartographic data, to the public administration information systems (§ 22 paras. 3 and 4) shall be determined by the Ministry of Agriculture in cooperation with the Ministry of the Environment by decree.

(3) The method of defining hydrogeological districts, defining water bodies, the method of evaluating their status, and the method of evaluating the ecological potential of heavily modified and artificial water bodies (§ 23a), the particulars of programs for assessing and evaluating the status of waters (§ 26 para. 4) shall be determined by the Ministry of the Environment and the Ministry of Agriculture by decree.

(4) The assessment and evaluation of the status of surface and groundwaters and the operation of public administration information systems are carried out by river basin administrators and other expert bodies, which are authorized, established, or founded for this purpose by the Ministry of Agriculture, or the Ministry of the Environment (hereinafter "authorized expert bodies"). River basin administrators and authorized expert bodies are obliged to follow the instructions of their founder or establishing body in this activity.

(5) River basin administrators and authorized expert bodies are entitled to request, for the purposes of assessing and evaluating the status of surface and groundwaters, information from those who manage surface or groundwaters, as well as from administrative authorities, or bodies of local self-government, within whose competence the permitting of the management of said waters falls, or who maintain information systems under special legal regulations;¹⁴) they are obliged to provide data free of charge to the river basin administrators and authorized expert bodies, or the river basin administrators and authorized expert bodies may collect this data from them free of charge and with their assistance. The provisions of special legal regulations protecting classified information are not affected by this.

(6) River basin administrators and authorized expert bodies shall, upon request, provide information on the status of surface and groundwaters to administrative authorities free of charge; at the same time, they shall provide free of charge to the Ministry of Health information concerning the management of surface and groundwaters in the protection zones of natural medicinal sources and sources of natural mineral waters.

(7) Employees of river basin administrators and authorized expert bodies
a) are authorized, in the performance of their duties, including the collection of surface and groundwater samples, to enter foreign lands to the extent necessary and to enter foreign structures and other premises used for business activities or the operation of other economic activities, if a permit under other legal regulations is not required for this; the owners or users of these premises are obliged to permit entry,
b) are obliged to present an authorization or an identity card of the river basin administrator or the authorized expert body and, before entering foreign lands or foreign structures and other premises, to inform the entitled person, as well as their owner or user.

§ 22

(1) The water balance consists of a hydrological balance and a water management balance. The hydrological balance compares the inflows and outflows of water and changes in water reserves of a river basin, territory, or water body for a given time interval. The water management balance compares the requirements for surface and groundwater abstractions and wastewater discharges with the usable capacity of water resources in terms of quantity and quality and their ecological status. The content of the water balance and the method of its preparation shall be determined by the Ministry of Agriculture in cooperation with the Ministry of the Environment by decree.

(2) For the needs of the water balance, anyone who is obliged under § 10 para. 1 or 2 to measure the quantity of water they manage, and further anyone who has a permit for the discharge of wastewater or the discharge of mine water into surface or groundwaters in a quantity exceeding 6,000 m³ in a calendar year or 500 m³ in a calendar month, is obliged to report once a year to the relevant river basin administrators data on this management or discharge in the manner and to the extent determined by the Ministry of Agriculture in cooperation with the Ministry of the Environment and the Ministry of Health by decree.

(3) The Ministry of Agriculture manages the public administration information system under § 21 para. 2 let. c) for the records of
a) water lines and objects on them and water reservoirs,
b) abstractions of surface and groundwaters, discharges of wastewater and mine water, and the accumulation of surface waters in water reservoirs,
c) international river basin districts in the territory of the Czech Republic and sub-basins (§ 24),
d) sources of surface and groundwaters that are used or are expected to be used as sources of drinking water,
e) main drainage and main irrigation facilities (§ 56).

(4) The Ministry of the Environment manages the public administration information system under § 21 para. 2 let. c) for the records of
a) objects on the water lines of hydrological river basins and hydrogeological districts,
b) water bodies, including heavily modified and artificial water bodies,
c) the quantity and quality of surface and groundwaters, the status of water bodies, and the ecological potential of heavily modified and artificial water bodies,
d) protected areas of natural water accumulation,
e) protection zones of water resources,
f) sensitive areas,
g) vulnerable areas,
h) areas of surface waters used for bathing,
i) floodplains,
j) surface waters that are or are intended to become permanently suitable for the life and reproduction of native species of fish and other aquatic animals.

(5) The Ministry of the Environment manages, as a separate component of the public administration information system under § 21 para. 2 let. c), a register of protected areas, in which, in connection with surface or groundwater bodies, it records areas and territories requiring special protection under this Act or the Act on Nature and Landscape Protection¹⁴a).

(6) The Ministry of Agriculture and the Ministry of the Environment shall proceed in the management of the information systems under paragraphs 3 and 4 in accordance with a special legal regulation.¹⁵) These information systems serve in particular for the purposes under § 21 para. 1, §§ 23 to 26, § 54, and § 108 para. 3 let. w).

TITLE IV
PLANNING IN THE WATER SECTOR

§ 23

(1) Planning in the water sector is a systematic conceptual activity ensured by the state, and its purpose is to define and mutually harmonize public interests in
a) the protection of waters as a component of the environment,
b) reducing the adverse effects of floods and droughts, and
c) the sustainable use of water resources, especially for the purpose of drinking water supply.

(2) Within the framework of planning in the water sector, river basin plans and flood risk management plans are prepared. These plans are the basis for the performance of public administration, especially for land-use planning and water management proceedings.

§ 23a
Objectives of Water Protection as a Component of the Environment

(1) The objectives of water protection as a component of the environment (hereinafter "water protection objectives") are
a) for surface waters

preventing the deterioration of the status of all bodies of these waters, including water bodies located in the same international river basin district,

ensuring the protection, improvement, and restoration of all bodies of these waters and achieving their good status, with the exception of the bodies mentioned in point 3,

ensuring the protection, improvement of the status of all artificial and heavily modified water bodies, and achieving their good ecological potential and good chemical status,

reducing their pollution by priority substances and stopping or gradually eliminating emissions, discharges, and leaks of priority hazardous substances,
b) for groundwaters

preventing or limiting the input of hazardous, particularly hazardous, and other harmful substances into these waters and preventing the deterioration of the status of all bodies of these waters,

ensuring the protection, improvement, and restoration of all bodies of these waters and ensuring a balanced state between groundwater abstractions and their replenishment, with the aim of achieving a good status of these waters,

reversing any significant and sustained upward trend in the concentration of hazardous, particularly hazardous, and other harmful substances as a result of the impact of human activity, for the purpose of effective reduction of the pollution of these waters,
c) also in the areas defined in § 28 para. 1, § 30 para. 1, § 32 para. 2, § 33 para. 1, § 34 para. 1, and § 35 para. 1, and in specially protected areas under special laws³¹) achieving the objectives set for surface waters under letter a) and for groundwaters under letter b), unless different requirements are set for these waters in these areas by special legal regulations.

(2) The objectives listed in paragraph 1 let. a) points 2 and 3, let. b) point 2, and let. c) must be achieved by 22 December 2015.

(3) If more than one water protection objective listed in paragraph 1 applies to a selected water body, the most stringent one shall always apply.

(4) For selected water bodies, special water protection objectives may be specified in the river basin plans (§ 24), which consist of extending the deadline specified in paragraph 2 for the purpose of gradually achieving the water protection objectives for water bodies or in setting less stringent water protection objectives.

(5) The deadline specified in paragraph 2 may be extended only if there is no further deterioration of the status of the affected water body and if these conditions are met:
a) the timely achievement of water protection objectives is not possible for at least one of the following reasons:

the degree of required improvement can, for reasons of technical feasibility, be achieved only by gradual steps that exceed the deadlines set by this Act,

achieving the required improvement within the deadline set by this Act would be disproportionately costly,

natural conditions do not allow for the timely improvement of the status of the given water body within the deadline set by this Act,
b) the extension of the deadline and the reasons for its extension will be specifically stated and explained in the river basin plan, and
c) the extension of the deadline will be limited to a period of a maximum of two subsequent updates of the river basin plans, with the exception of cases where natural conditions are such that the set water protection objectives cannot be achieved in these periods.

(6) Less stringent water protection objectives for selected water bodies may be set only if these water bodies are affected by human activity to the extent determined in accordance with § 25 para. 1 let. a) point 2, or if their natural conditions are such that achieving these objectives would be infeasible or disproportionately costly, and if these conditions are met:
a) the needs of the environment and socio-economic needs provided by such human activity cannot be achieved by other means that would be significantly better from an environmental perspective and would not require disproportionate costs,
b) for surface waters, the best possible ecological and chemical status will be achieved given the impacts that could not be prevented due to the nature of the human activity or pollution,
c) for groundwaters, the smallest possible change from a good groundwater status will be achieved given the impacts that could not be prevented due to the nature of the human activity or pollution,
d) there will be no further deterioration of the status of the affected water body, and
e) the setting of less stringent water protection objectives and the relevant reasons will be specifically stated and explained in the river basin plan, and these objectives will be reviewed every six years.

(7) Good status of groundwaters, good ecological status, good ecological potential, or preventing the deterioration of the status of a surface or groundwater body need not be achieved as a result of new changes in physical conditions in a surface water body or changes in the levels of groundwater bodies. A deterioration of the status of a surface water body from very good to good may occur as a result of new sustainable human activities.

(8) A deterioration of the status or ecological potential of a surface water body or the status of a groundwater body or making it impossible to achieve good status or good ecological potential of a surface water body or good status of a groundwater body under paragraph 7 is possible only on the basis of an exemption granted by the water authority upon application, while simultaneously fulfilling these conditions:
a) all feasible steps are taken to mitigate the adverse impacts on the status of the water body,
b) the reasons for these changes or modifications arise from an overriding public interest or if the benefits to the environment and society in achieving the objectives under paragraph 1 are outweighed by the benefits of the new modifications for human health, the maintenance of human safety, or sustainable development, and
c) the beneficial objectives which are served by these changes or modifications to the water body cannot, for reasons of technical infeasibility or disproportionate costs, be achieved by other means, which would be significantly better from an environmental perspective.

(9) Without a granted exemption under paragraph 8, a project leading to a deterioration of the status or ecological potential of a surface water body or the status of a groundwater body or making it impossible to achieve good status or good ecological potential of a surface water body or good status of a groundwater body cannot be permitted or carried out.

(10) The reasons for granting an exemption under paragraph 8 must be stated and explained in the current river basin plan under § 24 or in its next update.

(11) The deadline under paragraph 5 can be extended, less stringent objectives under paragraph 6 can be set, and an exemption under paragraph 8 can be granted, only if it does not lead to the permanent exclusion of or derogation from the achievement of the objectives of water protection as a component of the environment in other water bodies located in the same river basin district and their use is in accordance with the objectives of environmental protection.

§ 24
River Basin Plans

(1) The territory of the Czech Republic belongs to three international river basin districts, namely the Elbe international river basin district, the Oder international river basin district, and the Danube international river basin district.

(2) River basin plans under § 23 para. 2 are prepared at three levels: for international river basin districts (hereinafter "international river basin plans"), parts of international river basin districts in the territory of the Czech Republic (hereinafter "national river basin plans"), and sub-basins.

(3) The Ministry of the Environment and the Ministry of Agriculture cooperate within the framework of international commissions¹⁶) in the preparation of international river basin plans and international flood risk management plans or a set of flood risk management plans coordinated at the level of the international river basin district.

(4) National river basin plans set objectives:
a) for the protection and improvement of the status of surface and groundwaters and aquatic ecosystems,
b) for reducing the adverse effects of floods and droughts,
c) for the management of surface and groundwaters and the sustainable use of these waters to ensure water management services, and
d) for improving water conditions and for protecting the ecological stability of the landscape.
They also contain summaries of programs of measures to achieve the stated objectives and determine the strategy for their financing.

(5) The national river basin plan for the Elbe is supplemented by river basin plans for five sub-basins, namely for the sub-basin of the Upper and Middle Elbe, the sub-basin of the Upper Vltava, the sub-basin of the Berounka, the sub-basin of the Lower Vltava, and the sub-basin of the Ohře, Lower Elbe, and other tributaries of the Elbe.

(6) The national river basin plan for the Oder is supplemented by river basin plans for two sub-basins, namely for the sub-basin of the Upper Oder, the sub-basin of the Lusatian Neisse, and other tributaries of the Oder.

(7) The national river basin plan for the Danube is supplemented by river basin plans for three sub-basins, namely for the sub-basin of the Morava and tributaries of the Váh, the sub-basin of the Dyje, and the sub-basin of other tributaries of the Danube.

(8) The sub-basin plans determine proposals for programs of measures that are necessary to achieve the objectives for the given sub-basin based on the assessed status of surface and groundwaters, the assessment of flood risks, the needs of using water resources, and a time plan for their implementation.

(9) The Ministry of Agriculture shall, by decree, define the individual parts of the international river basin districts in the territory of the Czech Republic, the individual sub-basins under paragraphs 5 to 7 and the assigned hydrogeological districts, and also into which administrative districts of regions and administrative districts of municipalities with extended powers and into the territorial competence of which river basin administrators they fall.

(10) National river basin plans are prepared by the Ministry of Agriculture and the Ministry of the Environment in cooperation with the relevant river basin administrators and locally competent regional authorities. National river basin plans are approved by the government.

(11) Flood risk management plans are prepared by the Ministry of the Environment and the Ministry of Agriculture in cooperation with the relevant river basin administrators and locally competent regional authorities. Flood risk management plans are approved by the government.

(12) National river basin plans and flood risk management plans are integrated into the international plans under paragraph 3.

(13) Sub-basin plans are prepared by river basin administrators according to their competence in cooperation with the relevant regional authorities and in cooperation with the central water authorities. Sub-basin plans are approved by the regions according to their territorial competence.

§ 25
Preparation of River Basin Plans and Flood Risk Management Plans

(1) River basin plans and flood risk management plans are prepared in three stages, which consist of:
a) preparatory work, which must include

a preliminary assessment of flood risks and the definition of areas with significant flood risk, which must be published and made available to the public for comments, at least 4 years before the beginning of the period to which the flood risk management plans will apply,

a timetable and work program for the preparation of river basin plans, which must be published and made available to water users and the public for comments, at least 3 years before the beginning of the period to which the river basin plans will apply,

an analysis of the general and water management characteristics of the river basin, an assessment of the impacts of human activity on the status of surface and groundwaters, flood hazard maps and flood risk maps for the areas defined under point 1, an economic analysis of water use, and based on these, a prepared preliminary overview of significant water management problems identified in the river basin, including the identification of artificial water bodies, the determination of heavily modified water bodies and its justification, and proposals for special water protection objectives, which must be published and made available to water users and the public for comments, at least 2 years before the beginning of the period to which the river basin plans and flood risk management plans will apply,
b) the preparation of draft river basin plans and draft flood risk management plans, which must be prepared based on the results of the preparatory work and must contain programs of measures to achieve the objectives under § 24 para. 4, published and made available to water users and the public for comments at least 1 year before the beginning of the period to which the river basin plans and flood risk management plans will apply,
c) the preparation of river basin plans and flood risk management plans, revised according to the evaluation of consultations with water users and the public.

(2) The Ministry of Agriculture and the Ministry of the Environment shall, by decree, determine the content of river basin plans and flood risk management plans, the method of plan preparation, the details of the preparation stages under paragraph 1 including the method and form of preparing the preliminary assessment of flood risks, the method of determining areas with significant flood risk, the content and method of preparing flood hazard maps and flood risk maps and the form of their publication, the method of making preparatory work and draft river basin plans and draft flood risk management plans available for the active involvement of water users and the public.

(3) River basin plans and flood risk management plans are reviewed and updated every 6 years from the date of their approval according to the procedures specified in paragraphs 1 and 2.

(4) National river basin plans are issued by the Ministry of Agriculture as a measure of a general nature.

(5) Flood risk management plans are issued by the Ministry of the Environment as a measure of a general nature.

§ 26
Programs of Measures

(1) Programs of measures are the main tool for achieving the objectives stated in the river basin plans and flood risk management plans. Measures adopted to achieve water protection objectives in the program of measures must be implemented within 3 years of the approval of the river basin plans.

(2) Programs of measures to achieve water protection objectives must include basic measures and, where necessary, supplementary measures. The definition of the content of basic and supplementary measures and procedures for implementing measures, including the setting of more stringent water protection objectives and additional measures, shall be determined by the Ministry of Agriculture and the Ministry of the Environment by decree.
