(3) Measures adopted in the flood risk management plans must not, by their scope and impact, significantly increase flood risks downstream or upstream of the watercourse, unless such measures have been coordinated and agreed upon within the parts of international river basin districts in the territory of the Czech Republic or within international river basin districts.

(4) If the assessment and evaluation of the status of surface and groundwaters under § 21 or other data indicate that the water protection objectives set for the relevant water body under § 23a will likely not be achieved, it is necessary to
a) investigate the causes of the possible failure to comply,
b) review the corresponding permits for the management of waters to which § 12 para. 3 let. a) applies,
c) review and revise the programs for assessing and evaluating the status of surface and groundwaters,
d) adopt additional measures to achieve these water protection objectives, including the setting of more stringent values for selected indicators, or establish additional indicators, if it is effective.

(5) In cases of temporary deterioration of the status of water bodies due to natural causes or force majeure, which are exceptional or could not have been reasonably foreseen, such as in the case of extreme floods or periods of prolonged drought or as a result of accidents, these conditions must be met:
a) all appropriate measures must be taken to prevent further deterioration of the status and not to deviate from achieving the water protection objectives under § 23a para. 1 for other water bodies not affected by these extraordinary circumstances,
b) the conditions under which circumstances can be designated as extraordinary or reasonably unforeseeable are stated, including the introduction of relevant indicators, in the river basin plan,
c) the measures to be taken under such extraordinary circumstances are included in the programs of measures and will not compromise the recovery of the quality of the given water body after the end of the extraordinary circumstances,
d) the effects of extraordinary or reasonably unforeseeable circumstances are reviewed annually and, taking into account the reasons for extending the deadlines set in § 23a para. 5 and setting less stringent objectives in § 23a para. 6, all feasible measures are taken to restore the status of the water body as it was before the extraordinary circumstance, in the shortest possible time, and
e) a summary of the effects of the extraordinary circumstances and the measures that were or are to be taken in accordance with letters a) and d) are included in the next update of the river basin plan.

(6) The implementation of measures under paragraph 2 must not lead to the deterioration of the pollution of coastal and marine waters or to an increase in the pollution of surface waters. This requirement does not apply if its consequence would be an increased pollution of the environment as a whole.

(7) The Ministry of Agriculture, in cooperation with the Ministry of the Environment and regional authorities, submits to the government every 3 years a summary report on the implementation of the programs of measures and on the status of surface and groundwaters and water management in the river basin districts.

TITLE V
PROTECTION OF WATER CONDITIONS AND WATER RESOURCES

Division 1
Protection of Water Conditions

§ 27

Owners of land are obliged, unless a special legal regulation provides otherwise,¹⁸) to ensure the care of their land in such a way that there is no deterioration of water conditions. In particular, they are obliged under these conditions to ensure that there is no deterioration of runoff conditions, soil loss due to water erosion, and to strive to improve the retention capacity of the landscape.

§ 28
Protected Areas of Natural Water Accumulation

(1) Areas that, due to their natural conditions, form a significant natural accumulation of water are declared by the government by a regulation as protected areas of natural water accumulation.

(2) In protected areas of natural water accumulation, to the extent determined by the government regulation, it is prohibited to
a) reduce the extent of forest lands,
b) drain forest lands,
c) drain agricultural lands,
d) extract peat,
e) extract minerals by surface mining or carry out other earthworks that would lead to the uncovering of a continuous groundwater level,
f) extract and process radioactive raw materials,
g) dispose of radioactive waste,
h) store carbon dioxide⁴⁹) in hydrogeological structures with usable or utilized groundwater reserves.

(3) The Ministry of the Environment may, with the prior consent of the government, permit an exemption from the prohibitions listed in paragraph 2.

(4) If damage is caused to the owner of the land by the prohibition under paragraph 2 let. a) to c), they are entitled to its compensation.

§ 28a
Areas Designated for Surface Water Accumulation

(1) Areas that are morphologically, geologically, and hydrologically suitable for the accumulation of surface waters for reducing the adverse effects of floods and droughts may be defined in the Spatial Development Policy and in land-use planning documentation as areas designated for surface water accumulation to protect them from other activities. In these areas, existing land use may be changed, structures may be located, and other activities may be carried out only if they do not prevent or substantially hinder their future use for surface water accumulation.

(2) The General Plan of Areas Designated for Surface Water Accumulation and the basic principles for the use of these areas shall be prepared by the Ministry of Agriculture in agreement with the Ministry of the Environment. The General Plan is the basis for the draft Spatial Development Policy¹⁸a) and land-use planning documentation.

Division 2
Groundwaters

§ 29

(1) Groundwater resources are preferentially reserved for the supply of drinking water to the population and for purposes for which the use of drinking water is stipulated by a special legal regulation.⁵) The water authority may permit the use of groundwater for other purposes only if it is not to the detriment of satisfying the stated needs. The storage of carbon dioxide⁴⁹) in hydrogeological structures with significant reserves of quality groundwater intended primarily for the supply of drinking water to the population is prohibited.

(2) A person who, during their operational activity,¹⁹) causes the loss of groundwater or a substantial reduction in the possibility of its abstraction from a groundwater source, or a deterioration of its quality, is obliged to compensate for the damage caused thereby to the person who is permitted to abstract groundwater from this water source, and further to take the necessary measures according to local conditions to restore the original state. The compensation consists of providing a substitute water source. If this is not possible or expedient, they are obliged to provide a one-time compensation corresponding to the decrease in the value of this immovable property, with the use of which the permit is associated. Disputes over compensation for damages or its amount are decided by a court. General regulations on compensation for damages are not affected by this.

(3) The owner of a land who, during an activity other than geological works²⁰) on it, discovers the occurrence of groundwater in an unusual quantity (e.g., in such a quantity that requires a change in the technology of foundation engineering or necessitates the abandonment of the construction at this site, etc.) or discovers the occurrence of groundwater with an artesian head (artesian water), is obliged to report this fact to the relevant water authority to determine the yield of the groundwater source.

Division 3
Protection of Water Resources

§ 30
Protection Zones of Water Resources

(1) To protect the yield, quality, and health safety of groundwater or surface water sources used or usable for the supply of drinking water with an average abstraction of more than 10,000 m³ per year and groundwater sources for the production of bottled infant or spring water, the water authority shall establish protection zones by a measure of a general nature. If serious circumstances so require, the water authority may establish protection zones for water sources with a lower capacity than that stated in the first sentence. The water authority may, for serious reasons, change, or possibly abolish, a protection zone. The establishment of protection zones is always in the public interest.

(2) Protection zones are divided into protection zones of the I. degree, which serve to protect the water source in the immediate vicinity of the intake or abstraction facility, and protection zones of the II. degree, which serve to protect the water source in areas determined by the water authority, so that its yield, quality, or health safety is not endangered.

(3) The protection zone of the I. degree shall be established by the water authority as a continuous area
a) for water supply reservoirs and for other reservoirs intended exclusively for the supply of drinking water, at least for the entire area of the reservoir's water level at maximum impoundment,
b) for other reservoirs with water supply use other than those mentioned under letter a), with a minimum distance of the boundary of its definition on the reservoir's water level of 100 m from the abstraction facility,
c) for watercourses

with a weir impoundment on the bank of the abstraction, at least for a length of 200 m upstream from the abstraction point, downstream to a distance of 100 m or to the edge of the impounding structure, and a width of the protection zone of 15 m; in the watercourse, it includes at least one half of its width at the abstraction point,

without a weir impoundment on the bank of the abstraction, at least for a length of 200 m upstream from the abstraction point, downstream to a distance of 50 m from the abstraction point, and a width of the protection zone of 15 m; in the watercourse, it includes at least one-third of its width at the abstraction point,
d) for groundwater sources with a minimum distance of its defined boundary of 10 m from the abstraction facility,
e) in other cases individually.

(4) The water authority may, in justified cases, establish a protection zone of the I. degree in a smaller scope than that specified in paragraph 3 let. a) to d).

(5) The protection zone of the II. degree is established outside the protection zone of the I. degree; it may consist of one continuous area or several separate areas within a hydrological basin or hydrogeological district. The water authority may establish the protection zone of the II. degree, if it is expedient, gradually for individual areas.

(6) The water authority establishes protection zones at the proposal or on its own initiative. If those who have the right to abstract water from the water source, or who apply for a permit for such an abstraction, do not submit a proposal for their establishment, and for water supply reservoirs, those who own the waterworks serving for the impoundment of water in such reservoirs or are their builders, the water authority may impose on them the obligation to submit this proposal with the necessary documents. Reservoirs listed in the list under paragraph 13 are considered water supply reservoirs according to the preceding sentence.

(7) Entry and passage into the protection zone of the I. degree are prohibited; this does not apply to persons who have the right to abstract water from the water source, and for water supply reservoirs, to persons who own these waterworks. The water authority may, by a decision or a measure of a general nature, also grant other exemptions from the prohibition of entry and passage.

(8) In the protection zones of the I. and II. degree, it is prohibited to carry out activities that damage or endanger the yield, quality, or health safety of the water source, the scope of which is defined in the measure of a general nature on the establishment or change of the protection zone.

(9) If the reason for protection ceases to exist, the water authority shall abolish the protection zone by a measure of a general nature.

(10) In the measure of a general nature on the establishment or change of the protection zone of a water source, the water authority shall determine which activities that damage or endanger the yield, quality, or health safety of the water source cannot be carried out in this zone, what technical measures persons under paragraph 12 are obliged to take in the protection zone, and, where applicable, the manner and duration of the restriction on the use of lands and structures located in this zone.

(11) For the proven restriction on the use of lands and structures in the protection zones of water resources, the owners or tenants or lessees of these lands and structures are entitled to compensation, which, at their request, must be provided by the owners of the waterworks enabling the impoundment of water in them in the case of water supply reservoirs, and in other cases by those entitled (§ 8) to abstract water from the water source; if there are more of them, in proportion to the permitted quantity of abstracted water. If no agreement is reached on the provision of compensation, a court shall decide on a one-time compensation.

(12) The costs associated with technical modifications in the protection zones of water resources imposed by the water authority to protect the yield, quality, and health safety are borne by those who are entitled to abstract water from these water sources, or who apply for a permit for its abstraction, and for water supply reservoirs, by the owners or builders of the waterworks serving for the impoundment of water.

(13) The Ministry of the Environment shall, by decree, determine a list of water supply reservoirs and principles for the establishment and change of protection zones of water resources.

§ 31

For sources of surface waters that are used or are expected to be used as a source of drinking water, the indicators and values of their permissible pollution shall be determined by the government by a regulation.

§ 32
Sensitive Areas

(1) Sensitive areas are surface water bodies,
a) in which eutrophication occurs or may occur in the near future as a result of a high concentration of nutrients,
b) which are used or are expected to be used as a source of drinking water, in which the concentration of nitrates exceeds 50 mg/l, or
c) for which a higher degree of wastewater treatment is necessary from the perspective of the interests protected by this Act.

(2) Sensitive areas shall be defined by the government by a regulation. The definition of sensitive areas is subject to review at regular intervals not exceeding 4 years.

(3) For sensitive areas and for the discharge of wastewater into surface waters affecting the water quality in sensitive areas, the government shall, by a regulation, determine the indicators of permissible pollution of wastewater and their values.

§ 33
Vulnerable Areas

(1) Vulnerable areas are areas where
a) surface or groundwaters, especially those used or designated as a source of drinking water, in which the concentration of nitrates exceeds 50 mg/l or may reach this value, or
b) surface waters, in which an undesirable deterioration of water quality occurs or may occur as a result of a high concentration of nitrates from agricultural sources.

(2) The government shall, by a regulation, determine vulnerable areas and shall regulate in them the use and storage of fertilizers and farm manure, crop rotation, and the implementation of anti-erosion measures (hereinafter "action programme"). The action programme and the definition of vulnerable areas are subject to review and possible revision at intervals not exceeding 4 years. The review is carried out based on an evaluation of the effectiveness of the measures arising from the adopted action programme.

§ 34
Surface Waters Used for Bathing

(1) River basin administrators, in cooperation with the Ministry of the Environment, the Ministry of Health, water authorities, and the relevant regional hygienic stations, shall prepare, review, and update profiles of waters listed in the list of natural swimming pools operated on surface waters used for bathing and other surface waters where a large number of people can be expected to bathe⁴⁸). A profile of surface waters used for bathing is a summary of data on surface waters listed in the list compiled under the Act on the Protection of Public Health⁴⁸). A profile of surface waters used for bathing may be prepared for several adjacent surface waters. The content and method of preparing the profile of surface waters used for bathing, the conditions for its review and updating, and the scope and method of transmitting documents to the river basin administrators shall be determined by the Ministry of Agriculture in agreement with the Ministry of the Environment and the Ministry of Health by decree.

(2) The indicators and values of permissible pollution of waters for the purposes of permitting the discharge of wastewater into surface waters listed in the list compiled under the Act on the Protection of Public Health⁴⁸) and a programme for reducing the pollution of these waters to achieve the values of permissible pollution of these waters shall be determined by the government by a regulation.

(3) If surface waters listed in the list compiled under the Act on the Protection of Public Health⁴⁸) cease to comply permanently or repeatedly with the requirements for water quality for bathing, which are set by a special legal regulation or in the government regulation under paragraph 2, the water authority shall impose or adopt appropriate measures to remedy this situation, after consultation with the public health protection authorities and the river basin administrator. The surface waters listed in the list must meet the requirements for acceptable water quality by the end of the 2015 bathing season.

§ 35
Support for Fish Life

(1) Surface waters that are or are intended to become permanently suitable for the life and reproduction of native species of fish and other aquatic animals, with a division into salmonid and cyprinid waters, the indicators and values of permissible pollution of these waters, the method of assessing and evaluating the status of the quality of these waters, and a programme for reducing the pollution of these waters to achieve the values of permissible pollution of these waters shall be determined by the government by a regulation.

(2) For water supply or other water reservoirs or on sections of watercourses, the water authority may impose on their owner, the watercourse administrator, and the user of the fishing ground also the method of fishery management.

(3) The release of fish and other aquatic animals of genetically unsuitable and unverified populations of native species into watercourses and water reservoirs without the consent of the relevant water authority is prohibited. In the case of non-native species, the procedure is according to the Act on Nature and Landscape Protection¹⁴a).

Division 4
Protection of Water Quantity

§ 36
Minimum Residual Flow

(1) The minimum residual flow is the flow of surface waters that still allows for the general management of surface waters and the ecological functions of the watercourse and takes into account the possibilities of recreational navigation.

(2) The minimum residual flow is determined by the water authority in the permit for the management of waters. The water authority shall take into account the conditions of the watercourse and the possibilities of recreational navigation, the character of the management of waters, and shall base its decision on the measures to achieve the water protection objectives adopted in the river basin plan under § 26. It shall also determine the place and method of measuring the minimum residual flow and the frequency of submitting the results of these measurements to the water authority.

(3) The method and criteria for determining the minimum residual flow under paragraph 2 shall be determined by the government by a regulation.

(4) In the case of a waterwork under § 15a para. 3, if the conditions under § 15a para. 5 are met, the minimum residual flow is proposed in the project documentation. With the consent of the water authority to the notification of the waterwork, the proposal for the minimum residual flow stated in the project documentation is considered determined.

§ 37
Minimum Groundwater Levels

(1) The minimum groundwater level is a level that still allows for the sustainable use of water resources and ensures the achievement of a good ecological status of related surface water bodies and excludes significant damage to terrestrial ecosystems.

(2) The minimum groundwater level is determined by the water authority in the permit for the management of waters, if this management may result in a substantial lowering of the groundwater level. The water authority shall base its decision on the river basin plans and the methodological guideline issued by the Ministry of the Environment and shall take into account the assessed status of surface and groundwaters, especially the results of the water balance in the given hydrogeological district.

(3) The water authority may impose on the entitled person, within the meaning of paragraph 2, an obligation to submit a draft of an intake regulation for approval, or an obligation to regularly measure the groundwater level, the method of measurement, and an obligation to submit reports on the measurement results to the relevant river basin administrator.

Division 5
Water Quality Protection

§ 38
Wastewater

(1) Wastewater is water used in residential, industrial, agricultural, medical, and other buildings, facilities, or means of transport, which has altered quality (composition or temperature) after use, and its mixtures with stormwater, as well as other waters flowing from these buildings, facilities, or means of transport, if they can endanger the quality of surface or groundwaters. Wastewater also includes leachate originating from the operation of landfills and tailings ponds or during subsequent care for them, with the exception of waters that are reused for the organization's own needs, and waters that flow into mine waters.

(2) Wastewater treated at a municipal wastewater treatment plant, which is understood as a facility for treating urban wastewater equipped with technology for the disposal of sewage, must comply in its composition with the applicable sewer regulations.

(3) If wastewater and stormwater are drained together by a unified sewer system¹⁰a), the stormwater becomes wastewater upon inflow into this sewer system.

(4) Waters from drainage systems of drained agricultural lands, cooling waters used on vessels and for water turbines, where only the temperature has increased, and unused mineral waters from a natural medicinal source or a source of natural mineral water are not considered wastewater under this Act. Stormwater from road communications is also not wastewater, provided that the contamination of these waters with harmful substances is addressed by technical measures according to the decree implementing the Act on Road Communications²¹a).

(5) For the purposes of this Act, the treatment of wastewater means its discharge into surface or groundwaters or accumulation with its subsequent removal to a wastewater treatment plant under paragraph 8. Whoever discharges wastewater into surface or groundwaters is obliged to ensure its treatment in accordance with the conditions set in the permit for its discharge. When setting these conditions, the water authority is obliged to take into account the best available technologies in the field of wastewater treatment, which are understood as the most effective and advanced stage of development of the used technology for treatment or purification of wastewater, developed on a scale that allows for its implementation under economically and technically acceptable conditions and is at the same time the most effective for water protection. Whoever discharges mine water into surface or groundwaters under the Act on the Protection and Utilization of Mineral Wealth¹a) may do so only in the manner and under the conditions determined by the water authority.

(6) Whoever discharges wastewater into surface or groundwaters is obliged, in accordance with the decision of the water authority, to measure the volume of discharged water and the degree of its pollution and to submit the results of these measurements to the water authority that issued the decision, the relevant river basin administrator, and the authorized expert body. The water authority shall, by this decision, determine the place and method of measuring the volume and pollution of discharged wastewater and the frequency of submitting the results of these measurements. Sampling and analyses to determine the degree of pollution of discharged wastewater may only be carried out by professionally competent persons authorized to conduct business (hereinafter "accredited laboratory"). Professional competence for the analysis of wastewater and the performance of sampling is demonstrated by an accreditation certificate issued under the Act on Technical Requirements for Products⁵⁷), a certificate of correct laboratory practice, or an authorization to perform official measurements under the Metrology Act⁵⁸), relating to the analytical determination of relevant indicators and the collection of the required type of wastewater samples.

(7) The obligation under paragraph 6 does not apply to a person who treats wastewater through a waterwork intended for the treatment of wastewater up to a capacity of 50 population equivalents notified under § 15a, the essential component of which is a CE-marked product. The list and classification of CE-marked products, including the minimum treatment efficiency for categories of CE-marked products in percentages, shall be determined by the government by a regulation.

(8) Whoever accumulates wastewater in a sealed tank is obliged to ensure its treatment by removal to a wastewater treatment plant and, at the request of the water authority or the Czech Environmental Inspectorate, to present documents on the removal of wastewater for the period of the last two calendar years. The removal may only be carried out by the operator of a wastewater treatment plant or a person authorized under the Trade Licensing Act²³). The person who carries out the removal is obliged to issue a document to the person who accumulates wastewater in a sealed tank, from which the name of the person who accumulates wastewater in the sealed tank, the location of the tank, the quantity of removed wastewater, the date of removal, the name of the person who removed the wastewater, and the name of the wastewater treatment plant to which the wastewater will be treated, will be apparent.

(9) The direct discharge of wastewater into groundwaters is prohibited. The discharge of wastewater not containing hazardous harmful substances or particularly hazardous harmful substances (§ 39 para. 3) from one or several geographically related residential buildings⁵⁰), buildings for family recreation⁵¹), or from individual buildings providing accommodation services⁵²), originating mainly as a product of human metabolism and activities in households, through soil layers into groundwaters may be permitted if, in the given case, the discharge of wastewater into surface waters is not technically possible or desirable with regard to the interests protected by this Act or other legal regulations. A permit for the discharge of wastewater into groundwaters under the second sentence cannot be issued without the consent of a person with professional competence⁸), who assesses the impact of the wastewater discharge on the quality of groundwaters. The maximum permitted quantity of wastewater discharged from one or several geographically related residential buildings must not exceed a total of 15 m³/day.

(10) When permitting the discharge of wastewater into surface or groundwaters, the water authority shall set the maximum permissible values for the quantity and concentration of discharged pollution (emission limits) and the volume of discharged water. When permitting the discharge of wastewater into surface waters, it is bound by the indicators expressing the status of the water in the watercourse, environmental quality standards, indicators and values of permissible pollution of surface waters, indicators and maximum permissible values of wastewater pollution indicators (emission standards) established by a government regulation, and the particulars and conditions of the permit for the discharge of wastewater, including specifications of the best available technologies in the field of wastewater treatment and the conditions of their use, which are determined by a government regulation, and the best available techniques⁵⁹) in the field of wastewater treatment. When permitting the discharge of wastewater into groundwaters, it is bound by the indicators expressing the status of groundwater in the relevant groundwater body, indicators and values of permissible pollution of groundwaters, indicators and permissible values of wastewater pollution, and the particulars and conditions of the permit for the discharge of wastewater into groundwaters, which are determined by a government regulation.

(11) When permitting the discharge of wastewater into surface or groundwaters, the water authority
a) shall take into account the need to achieve or maintain a good status of surface or groundwaters and of water-dependent ecosystems, and
b) shall assess the possibilities of reducing pollution at its source and reducing emissions into the environment as a whole, and the possibility of reusing wastewater.

(12) If required by the objectives set in the relevant river basin plan or water protection objectives or environmental quality standards set by a directly applicable regulation of the European Union, the water authority shall, in the permit, set stricter emission limits than the emission limits set under paragraph 10, or it may set additional indicators and their emission limits. The emission limits set by the water authority must not be stricter than the values achievable by using the best available techniques in the field of wastewater treatment⁵⁹). The stated procedure applies mutatis mutandis to cases of setting pollution indicators and emission standards established by a government regulation under §§ 31, 34, and 35.

(13) The water authority may, when permitting the discharge of wastewater from industrial buildings and facilities, impose the obligation to treat wastewater from individual partial production units or cooling waters separately from other wastewater.

(14) The water authority may, at the request of the polluter, permit in exceptional cases for a strictly necessary period, especially when putting a wastewater treatment plant into operation, during trial operation, necessary repairs or changes to the wastewater treatment facility, and in case of accidents of these facilities, and in cases where wastewater will be discharged into surface waters in a controlled manner, while simultaneously setting other conditions that limit the possibility of deteriorating the quality of surface waters, the discharge of wastewater with permissible values of wastewater pollution indicators higher than the values set by a government regulation under paragraph 10 or under § 31.

(15) In case of doubt as to whether it is wastewater, the water authority shall decide.

§ 39
Harmful Substances

(1) Harmful substances are substances that are not wastewater or mine water and which may endanger the quality of surface or groundwaters (hereinafter "harmful substances"). Anyone who handles harmful substances is obliged to take appropriate measures to prevent them from entering surface or groundwaters and endangering their environment.

(2) In cases where the user of harmful substances handles these substances on a larger scale or where handling them is associated with an increased risk to surface or groundwaters, the user of harmful substances is obliged to take these measures:
a) prepare a plan of measures for cases of an accident (hereinafter "contingency plan") and submit it for approval to the relevant water authority; if an accident may affect a watercourse, the user of harmful substances shall discuss it with the relevant watercourse administrator, to whom they shall also provide one copy, before submitting it for approval,
b) keep records of the measures taken and retain these records for a period of 5 years.

(3) A list of hazardous harmful substances and other substances or groups of substances that cause similar concern is provided in Annex No. 1 to this Act; this list also includes particularly hazardous harmful substances. A special category of hazardous harmful substances are priority substances, which represent a significant risk to the aquatic environment and related ecosystems. The list of priority substances is determined by the government by a regulation. Part of the list of priority substances is also the category of priority hazardous substances, which are substances that pose a very high risk in the aquatic environment or indirectly through the aquatic environment due to their persistence and bioaccumulation capacity. To reduce the pollution of surface and groundwaters by hazardous harmful substances and particularly hazardous harmful substances, the government may, at the proposal of the Ministry of the Environment, adopt a Programme for reducing the pollution of surface and groundwaters by hazardous harmful substances and particularly hazardous harmful substances.

(4) Anyone who handles particularly hazardous harmful substances or hazardous harmful substances or who handles harmful substances on a larger scale or where handling them is associated with an increased risk, is obliged to take appropriate measures to prevent them from entering surface or groundwaters or sewer systems that are not part of the technological equipment of the production facility. They are obliged in particular to
a) locate facilities in which harmful substances are used, collected, stored, processed, or transported in such a way as to prevent the undesirable leakage of these substances into the soil or their undesirable mixing with wastewater or stormwater,
b) use only such equipment, or possibly a method of handling harmful substances, that are suitable also from the perspective of water quality protection,
c) inspect warehouses and landfills, including the outlets of their control systems, at least once every 6 months to detect the leakage of harmful substances and to promptly carry out their timely repairs; warehouses must be secured by an impermeable treatment against the leakage of harmful substances into groundwaters,
d) at least once every 5 years, unless a shorter period is specified by a technical standard or the manufacturer, test the tightness of pipelines or tanks intended for the storage and means of transport of particularly hazardous harmful substances and hazardous harmful substances by a professionally competent person, and in case of detected deficiencies, to promptly carry out their timely repairs; the tightness of tanks intended for the storage of oil or petroleum products with a minimum volume of 1000 m³ or used for the storage of oil and petroleum products under the Act on Emergency Oil Stocks²¹b), secured by an impermeable treatment against the leakage of harmful substances into groundwaters and continuously monitored by control systems, the outputs of which are recorded and stored until the next tightness test, may, unless a shorter period is specified by the manufacturer, be tested at least once every 20 years; in the case of storing fertilizers and leachates from bulk feed or substances intended for the treatment of water for drinking purposes and for the treatment of municipal wastewater in above-ground tanks located in containment basins with a volume greater than the volume of the largest tank located in them, a repeated tightness test is not required,
e) build and operate an appropriate control system for detecting the leakage of harmful substances and submit its outputs at the request of the water authority or the Czech Environmental Inspectorate,
f) ensure that newly constructed buildings are secured against the undesirable leakage of these substances during firefighting.

(5) The measures under paragraph 4 shall apply mutatis mutandis to the used packaging of harmful substances.

(6) Anyone who handles particularly hazardous harmful substances is obliged to keep records of the types of these substances that are processed or handled, of their quantity, of the content of their active components, of their properties, especially in relation to surface and groundwaters, and to provide this information upon request to the water authority and the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic.

(7) The water authority may, when using harmful substances, grant an exemption from the provisions of paragraph 1 and set conditions for their use, if it is not petroleum substances, to a strictly necessary extent, for a limited period, and on the condition that they will be used
a) for the regulation and maintenance of a watercourse bed,
b) for feeding fish,
c) for health reasons,
d) for the treatment of surface or groundwaters for specific uses, for example, the precipitation of inorganic nutrients directly in the watercourse,
e) for the removal of undesirable flora or fauna in the watercourse,
f) as indicator substances for measurement purposes, or
g) within approved remediation technologies.

(8) The particulars of the contingency plan and the handling of harmful substances, including requirements for a professionally competent person and containment basins under paragraph 4 let. d), shall be determined by the Ministry of the Environment by a decree. Principles for setting conditions for the use of harmful substances in the case of exemptions under paragraph 7 let. b), d), and e) and when managing waters for the purpose of farming fish or waterfowl, or possibly other aquatic animals, and the definition of categories of ponds from a fishery management perspective shall be determined by the Ministry of the Environment and the Ministry of Agriculture by a decree.

(9) The washing of motor vehicles and operational machinery in watercourses or at places where the quality of surface or groundwaters could be endangered is prohibited.

(10) The provisions of paragraphs 2, 4, and 5 apply mutatis mutandis to the handling of sedimentable solid substances listed in Annex No. 1 to this Act.

(11) The storage of carbon dioxide⁴⁹) in surface waters is prohibited.

(12) An exemption from the use of harmful substances is not required for the supplemental feeding of fish with feed of plant origin carried out in a pond in such a way that the quantity of administered feed is consumed by the fish stock, and thus no decomposition of the feed and the associated deterioration of water quality occurs. The feed used for these purposes must not contain hazardous or particularly hazardous harmful substances, and supplemental feeding without an exemption must not be carried out on surface waters listed in the list of natural swimming pools under the Act on the Protection of Public Health and on water supply reservoirs. For compliance with the conditions specified in the first and second sentences, it is not necessary to monitor water quality in the pond or at its outlet. In case of an inspection, the fish farmer shall present to the water authority or the Czech Environmental Inspectorate records of management kept under the Fisheries Act.

§ 40
Accident

(1) An accident is an extraordinary serious deterioration or an extraordinary serious threat to the quality of surface or groundwaters.

(2) Cases of serious deterioration or extraordinary threat to the quality of surface or groundwaters by petroleum substances, particularly hazardous harmful substances, or possibly radioactive emitters and radioactive waste, or if a deterioration or threat to the quality of surface or groundwaters occurs in protected areas of natural water accumulation or in protection zones of water resources, are always considered an accident.

(3) Furthermore, cases of technical failures and defects of facilities for the collection, storage, transport, and disposal of the substances listed in paragraph 2 are considered an accident, if they precede such an entry.

§ 41
Obligations in Case of an Accident

(1) The person who caused the accident (hereinafter "the originator of the accident") is obliged to take immediate measures to eliminate the causes and consequences of the accident. In doing so, they shall follow the contingency plan, or the instructions of the water authority and the Czech Environmental Inspectorate.

(2) Whoever causes or discovers an accident is obliged to immediately report it to the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic or fire protection units or the Police of the Czech Republic, or possibly the river basin administrator.

(3) The Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic, the Police of the Czech Republic, and the river basin administrator are obliged to immediately inform the relevant water authority and the Czech Environmental Inspectorate of the accident reported to them, which will also inform the Ministry of Health about accidents that occurred in the protection zones of natural medicinal sources and sources of natural mineral waters and on surface waters used under § 34. The management of work for the disposal of accidents belongs to the water authority, which shall immediately inform the river basin administrator of the accident.

(4) In the event of an accident of extraordinary scope, which may seriously endanger the lives or health of people or cause significant damage to property, the provisions on flood protection shall apply mutatis mutandis to the prevention of harmful consequences of the accident.

(5) The originator of the accident is obliged, at the request of the authorities listed in paragraph 3, to cooperate with these authorities in carrying out measures to eliminate the causes and consequences of the accident.

(6) Persons who participated in the disposal of the accident are obliged to provide the Czech Environmental Inspectorate with the necessary data, if it requests their provision, and to the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic.

(7) The Ministry of the Environment shall, by decree, determine the manner and scope of reporting accidents, their disposal, and the removal of their harmful consequences.

§ 42
Remedial Measures

(1) To remedy the consequences of an unauthorized discharge of wastewater, unauthorized handling of harmful substances, or an accident (hereinafter "defective state"), the water authority or the Czech Environmental Inspectorate shall impose on the person who violated the obligation to protect surface or groundwaters or on the originator of the accident (hereinafter "the originator of the defective state"), an obligation to carry out measures to remedy the defective state (hereinafter "remedial measures"), and, where applicable, also measures to ensure a substitute water abstraction, if the nature of the matter so requires. The costs of implementing the remedial measures are borne by the person on whom the remedial measures were imposed. If the person on whom the measures were imposed fails to comply with them and there is a risk of delay, the water authority or the Czech Environmental Inspectorate shall ensure the remedial measures at their expense. If the accident was caused as a result of an intervention by the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic or fire protection units, they are not considered the originator of the accident if they used appropriate means for the intervention.

(2) The water authority or the Czech Environmental Inspectorate shall, as needed, impose remedial measures on the acquirer of property acquired in a manner specified in a special act,²²) who is not the originator of the defective state, but to whose property thus acquired the defective state is attached. The water authority or the Czech Environmental Inspectorate shall proceed in this way if the acquirer of this property acquired it with knowledge of the ecological burden and if a special agreement was concluded with them on this matter.

(3) The obligations arising from the remedial measures imposed on the originator of the defective state or the acquirer of property under paragraph 2 pass to their legal successors.

(4) If remedial measures cannot be imposed under paragraphs 1 to 3 and there is a serious threat or pollution of surface or groundwaters, the relevant water authority shall ensure the necessary remedial measures on its own initiative or at the initiative of the Czech Environmental Inspectorate. For this purpose, it may impose the implementation of remedial measures on a legal person or a natural person conducting business under special legal regulations,²³) who is professionally and technically qualified to implement the remedial measures. Only this person is a party to the proceeding on the imposition of the measures; an appeal against this decision does not have a suspensive effect. For this purpose, the region establishes a special account within its budget, annually supplemented up to CZK 10,000,000.

(5) From the special account of the region established under paragraph 4, the reimbursement of costs for remedial measures to remedy environmental damage to surface or groundwaters under the Act on the prevention and remedying of environmental damage and on the amendment of certain acts²³a) may also be paid. The relevant region shall send these funds to the relevant authority under the Act on the prevention and remedying of environmental damage and on the amendment of certain acts without undue delay upon its request.

(6) Owners of property on which the defective state is attached or whose property must be used for the removal of the defective state and who are not the persons on whom the remedial measures were imposed, are obliged to tolerate the implementation of the remedial measures imposed or ordered by the water authority. For this purpose, they are obliged to allow entry, or possibly passage, onto their lands and structures and to tolerate the restriction of the usual use of their lands and structures.

(7) For entry, or possibly passage, into the structures and facilities of the armed forces of the Czech Republic, the Police of the Czech Republic, the Security Information Service, and the Prison Service of the Czech Republic, special legal regulations apply.²⁴)

(8) If the imposed remedial measures affect foreign lands or structures, the rights of the owners of the affected lands and structures must be respected as much as possible; entry, or possibly passage, and the intended restriction of the usual use of the lands or structures must be notified to them in advance, unless there is a risk of delay. After the completion of the remedial measures, those on whom the remedial measures were imposed are obliged to restore the lands or structures to their previous state at their own expense, unless they have agreed otherwise with their owners; if the remedial measures are carried out on the basis of a decision of the water authority under paragraph 4, these costs are paid by the relevant municipality, from state funds.

(9) Compensation for property damage or restriction incurred by owners during the implementation of remedial measures on their lands or structures is paid by the person on whom the remedial measures were imposed. In the case mentioned in paragraph 4, this compensation is paid by the relevant water authority. The right to compensation must be claimed from the person on whom the remedial measures were imposed, or from the relevant water authority, within 6 months of its occurrence, otherwise it expires. This provision does not affect the right to compensation for damages.

TITLE VI
WATERCOURSES

§ 43
Watercourses

(1) Watercourses are surface waters flowing under their own gradient in a bed permanently or for the predominant part of the year, including waters artificially impounded in them. Their components are also waters in oxbow lakes and in sections temporarily flowing through natural cavities under the earth's surface or covered sections.

(2) In case of doubt as to whether it is a watercourse, the water authority shall decide. It may also decide that other surface waters than those mentioned in paragraph 1 are watercourses.

(3) The provisions of a special act²⁵) concerning torrent control are not affected.

§ 44
Beds of Watercourses

(1) If a watercourse flows over a land that is registered in the Real Estate Cadastre as a water body, the bed of the watercourse is this land. If a watercourse flows over a land that is not registered in the Real Estate Cadastre as a water body, the bed of the watercourse is the part of the land comprising the bottom and banks of the bed up to the bank line determined by the water level that is usually sufficient to flow through this bed without overflowing into the adjacent area.

(2) The natural bed of a watercourse is a bed or its part that was created by the natural action of flowing surface waters and other natural factors or by the implementation of remedial measures for interventions caused by human activity or the removal of a waterwork for the purpose of restoring the natural bed of a minor watercourse, and which can change its direction, longitudinal slope, and cross-sectional profile.

(3) In case of doubt about the boundary of a watercourse bed or whether it is a natural watercourse bed, the locally competent water authority shall decide.

§ 45
Changes to a Watercourse Bed

(1) If a watercourse leaves its natural bed during a flood due to natural forces and a new bed is thereby created, the owners of the land, the watercourse administrator, as well as those with rights to manage the waters who are affected by the new state, may individually or jointly request a permit from the water authority to return the watercourse to its original bed at their own expense. The state may contribute to the restoration of the watercourse bed after a flood for applicants who receive a permit (§ 102).

(2) If the original state is not restored, the state shall purchase the land of the original or new watercourse bed if the owner of the affected land offers it to the state. This does not apply to affected lands owned by municipalities.

(3) If the original state is not restored because the water authority did not permit the restoration in the public interest, the owners of the affected lands are entitled to compensation under paragraph 2, and the other parties with rights to manage the waters, affected by this decision, are entitled to reasonable compensation.

(4) The right to restoration and compensation shall expire three years from the year in which the change occurred.

§ 46
Protection of Watercourses and their Beds

(1) It is prohibited to change the course, longitudinal slope, and cross-sectional profile of a watercourse bed, to damage banks, to extract soil, sand, or minerals from watercourse beds, and to deposit objects in watercourses that could endanger the smooth flow of water, health, or safety, as well as to deposit such objects in places from which they could be washed into the waters.

(2) The provision of the preceding paragraph does not apply to cases where the activities mentioned therein are carried out in accordance with this Act.

§ 47
Administration of Watercourses

(1) Watercourses are subject to administration. They are divided into significant watercourses and minor watercourses. The list of significant watercourses shall be determined by the Ministry of Agriculture in cooperation with the Ministry of the Environment by decree.

(2) The administration of watercourses is understood as the obligation to
a) monitor the condition of watercourse beds and riparian lands from the perspective of the watercourse's functions,
b) care for watercourse beds, maintain bank vegetation on the lands of watercourse beds or on lands adjacent to them within the width specified under § 49 para. 2, in such a way that they do not become an obstacle preventing the smooth flow of water during a flood, taking into account that their species composition should correspond as much as possible to the natural conditions of the given location; this does not apply if the lands are designated to fulfill forest functions,
c) operate and maintain in proper condition the waterworks in the watercourse beds that are necessary to ensure the functions of the watercourse,²⁶) or which predominantly serve the watercourse, and which the watercourse administrators own or use on other legal grounds,
d) prepare and ensure adjustments to watercourse beds, if they serve to ensure the functions of the watercourse,
e) create conditions enabling authorized water management associated with the watercourse; in extraordinary situations on the watercourse, only if hydrological conditions and the state of the watercourse permit,
f) notify the relevant water authority of serious defects found in the watercourse and its bed, caused by natural or other influences; at the same time, to propose remedial measures, to restore the natural beds of watercourses, especially in specially protected areas²⁷) and in systems of ecological stability,²⁸)
g) cooperate in the disposal of accidents on watercourses,
h) propose measures to remedy interventions caused by human activity leading to the restoration of the natural beds of watercourses,
i) restore the natural beds of minor watercourses by removing waterworks by which the beds of minor watercourses were regulated, changed, or established before the year 2002.

(3) The Ministry of Agriculture shall, by decree, determine the manner of carrying out the activities listed in paragraph 2.

(4) The administration of significant watercourses, in addition to the obligations of administering watercourses under paragraph 2, includes the following further obligations:
a) to operate and maintain in proper condition the waterworks on significant watercourses that ensure authorized management of surface waters, which the administrators of significant watercourses own, or which they use on other legal grounds,
b) to maintain the navigability of used waterways of transport importance, including the breaking up of ice formations in public ports established by decree, and to mark and buoy the navigation channel on waterways⁷); the Ministry of Agriculture and the Ministry of Transport shall, by decree, establish the public ports in which ice formations are broken up,
c) to maintain in proper condition and operate also other persons' waterworks on watercourses, if the water authority so decides (§ 59 para. 3),
d) to direct and influence, according to the complex manipulation plan, the management of water in the system of water reservoirs,
e) to submit proposals for the preparation, modification, and coordination of the manipulation rules of waterworks owned by others,
f) to cooperate in the disposal of accidents in the river basin, if the quality of water in significant watercourses may be endangered,
g) to submit for approval to the water authority, at its request, a proposal for a complex manipulation plan that coordinates the manipulation rules of individual waterworks forming a mutually influencing system of waterworks, and to propose to the water authorities amendments to permits for the management of waters if they are affected by the approved manipulation plan; the water authority is obliged to decide on such a proposal,
h) to cooperate with the administrators of minor watercourses in addressing tasks concerning watercourses throughout the river basin district.

(5) The administration of watercourses under paragraphs 2 and 4 must be carried out in such a way that the adverse impact on aquatic and water-dependent ecosystems is minimized, and with regard to achieving a good water status under § 23a para. 1 let. a) points 2 and 3.

§ 48
Administrators of Watercourses

(1) The administration of significant watercourses is ensured by legal entities established under a special act¹⁷) (hereinafter "river basin administrators"); for the purposes of this Act, they are considered administrators of watercourses.

(2) The administration of minor watercourses or their integral sections may be carried out by municipalities through whose territory the minor watercourses flow, or by natural or legal persons, or possibly state organizational units, to whom the minor watercourses serve or with whose activities they are related, or state enterprises, on the basis of a designation by the Ministry of Agriculture. The Ministry of Agriculture decides on the designation as an administrator and the revocation of an administrator of a minor watercourse on the basis of an application; this does not apply in the case of designating or revoking a state organizational unit or state enterprise as an administrator, whose object of business or activity is the administration of minor watercourses. Simultaneously with the designation of a state organizational unit or state enterprise as an administrator of a minor watercourse, for which the previous administrator was a state organizational unit or state enterprise, the right to manage the lands with the bed of such a watercourse, the waterworks associated with such a watercourse, and the lands under these waterworks, passes from the previous to the new administrator of the minor watercourse, if these properties are owned by the state.

(3) In the territory of military districts²⁹), the administration of minor watercourses is ensured by the Ministry of Defence. In the territory of national parks, the administration of minor watercourses is ensured by the National Park Administrations; for the purposes of this Act, the Ministry of Defence and the National Park Administrations are considered administrators of watercourses.

(4) On minor watercourses for which no administrator has been designated, their administration is carried out by the administrator of the watercourse to which the minor watercourse is a tributary, until such time as an administrator is designated under paragraph 2. This also applies if there is an integral section of a minor watercourse on a minor watercourse for which no administrator has been designated, for which an administrator has been designated.

(5) The content of the application under paragraph 2 and its particulars necessary for the issuance of the decision shall be determined by the Ministry of Agriculture by decree.

(6) The river basin administrator supervises the administration of minor watercourses. If the administrator of a minor watercourse fails to fulfill its obligations under this Act, the Ministry of Agriculture may, at the proposal of the river basin administrator, revoke the designation as an administrator of the minor watercourse.

§ 49
Rights in the Administration of Watercourses

(1) Administrators of watercourses are entitled
a) in the performance of their rights and duties, to enter and pass over foreign lands and structures to the necessary extent, if a permit under special legal regulations is not required,
b) for the purpose of caring for watercourse beds and after consultation with the landowners, to remove or newly plant trees and shrubs on lands adjacent to them within the width specified under paragraph 2,
c) to demand the submission of a permit or consent from the water authority concerning the watercourse and to ascertain whether these decisions are being complied with,
d) to give instructions for the manipulation of waterworks to their users within the framework of the complex manipulation plan for the system of water reservoirs on the watercourse, if an extraordinary situation so requires.
The exercise of these rights does not affect special legal regulations concerning nature and landscape protection.³¹)

(2) Administrators of watercourses may, in the performance of their administration of the watercourse, if it is strictly necessary and after prior consultation with the landowners, use the lands adjacent to the watercourse bed, specifically
a) for waterways of transport importance, up to a width of 10 m from the bank line,
b) for other significant watercourses other than under letter a), up to a width of 8 m from the bank line,
c) for minor watercourses, up to a width of 6 m from the bank line.

(3) The water authority may, for strictly necessary needs and for a strictly necessary period, determine a wider strip of land for use adjacent to the watercourse than that specified in paragraph 2.

(4) If the administrator of a watercourse causes damage in the exercise of their rights under paragraph 1 or 2, they are obliged to compensate for it. General regulations on compensation for damages apply.

§ 50
Obligations of Owners of Lands on which Watercourse Beds are Located

Owners of lands on which watercourse beds are located are obliged to
a) tolerate bank vegetation on their land, as well as the general management of waters in the watercourse,
b) maintain the banks of the watercourse bed in a state necessary to ensure the harmless flow of water, to remove obstacles and foreign objects in the watercourse, with the exception of deposits, if these activities do not require the expenditure of special costs, special expertise, or the use of special technology,
c) tolerate waterworks located in the watercourse bed on their land, which were built before the effective date of this Act,
d) report apparent defects in the watercourse bed to the watercourse administrator,
e) tolerate on their land, without compensation, the placement of equipment for monitoring the status of surface and groundwaters and the ecological functions of the watercourse, such as navigation signs, etc.,
f) allow the water authority, the Czech Environmental Inspectorate, as well as the watercourse administrator, to exercise their rights,
g) tolerate the passage of persons along the watercourses on their land; the water authority may grant an exception from this obligation after consultation with the relevant watercourse administrator; this does not apply to lands in built-up areas and on fenced lands,
h) tolerate the natural bed of the watercourse on their land.

§ 51
Obligations of Owners of Lands Adjacent to Watercourse Beds

(1) Owners of lands adjacent to watercourse beds are obliged to
a) allow the watercourse administrator to exercise their rights,
b) tolerate on their land, without compensation, the placement of equipment for monitoring the status of surface and groundwaters and the ecological functions of the watercourse, the placement of navigation signs, etc.,
c) tolerate, after prior consultation with them, the passage of persons over their land; this does not apply to lands in built-up areas and on fenced lands,
d) tolerate the natural bed of the watercourse on their land.

(2) The water authority may prohibit the owners of lands adjacent to watercourse beds from felling trees and shrubs that ensure the stability of the watercourse bed.

(3) If damage is caused to the landowner by the exercise of these rights, they are entitled to its compensation.

§ 52
Obligations of Owners of Structures and Facilities in or Adjacent to Watercourse Beds

(1) Owners of structures and facilities in watercourse beds are obliged to remove objects caught on or attached to these structures and facilities and to dispose of them according to a special act.³²)

(2) Owners of structures that are not waterworks, or facilities in watercourse beds, or adjacent to them, are obliged in the public interest to care for their static safety and overall maintenance so that they do not endanger the smooth flow of surface waters, and to secure them against damage caused by water and the passage of ice. If the smooth flow of water is disrupted as a result of neglecting the care of these structures or facilities, their owners are obliged to carry out remedial action at their own expense and to fully restore the smooth flow of water; otherwise, the water authority is entitled to ensure remedial action at the owner's expense; liability for damage caused by neglecting the duty of care for a structure or facility in or adjacent to a watercourse bed is not affected by this.

§ 53
Doubts about the Scope of Obligations and Rights

In case of doubt about the scope of the obligations or rights of river basin administrators and watercourse administrators, the regional authority shall decide. It shall also decide in case of doubt about the scope of the obligations of the owners of the land of a watercourse bed, the owners of lands adjacent to watercourse beds, and the owners of structures and facilities in or adjacent to a watercourse bed. If such a doubt arises in a water management proceeding in which the person whose obligations or rights are in doubt is a party, the water authority conducting such a proceeding shall decide.

TITLE VII
RIVER BASIN ADMINISTRATION

§ 54

(1) River basin administration is understood as the administration of significant watercourses (§ 47 para. 4), certain activities associated with the assessment and evaluation of the status of surface and groundwaters in the given river basin district (§ 21), and other activities carried out by river basin administrators under this Act.

(2) River basin administration is carried out by river basin administrators.

(3) River basin administrators shall provide, for the activities of water authorities and for the activities of the Czech Environmental Inspectorate under § 112, at their request, technical, economic, and other data, if they have it at their disposal.

(4) River basin administrators, within their activities, submit initiatives, proposals, and opinions to water authorities and other administrative authorities from the perspective of the interests given by the relevant plans in the water sector and from the perspective of other interests pursued by the Act, especially in matters of protecting water conditions, protecting waters, the sustainable use of water resources, minimum residual flows of watercourses, minimum groundwater levels, and during temporary water shortages. They also provide opinions of river basin administrators, especially for the issuance of a permit for the management of waters [§ 8 para. 1 let. a) to c)], including the assessment of proposals for emission limit values from the perspective of compliance with § 38 para. 10, for the issuance of a permit for certain selected activities [§ 14 para. 1 let. a) to c)], for the issuance of a building permit for waterworks (§ 15), for the notification of waterworks (§ 15a), for the granting of consent (§ 17), a binding opinion (§ 104 para. 9), and an exemption under § 23a para. 8, including the assessment of the possibility of deteriorating the status or ecological potential by the intended project on the affected water body or the impossibility of achieving good status or good ecological potential by the intended project on the affected water body (§ 23a para. 7), and the degree of flood hazard and flood threat [§ 17 para. 1 let. c)], and for the issuance of an opinion (§ 18), in which they assess the compliance of projects to locate, construct, change, or remove a structure, facility, or carry out other activities with the above-mentioned interests, if such projects could affect water conditions, energy potential, or the quality or quantity of surface or groundwaters.

(5) River basin administrators cooperate with the administrators of minor watercourses and authorized expert bodies in addressing tasks concerning the entire river basin district.

(6) River basin administrators record, within the relevant river basin district, the reduction of the retention capacity of floodplains due to changes in the territory³²a), especially the implementation of flood protection structures, and in the exercise of their powers, propose to the relevant authorities a method of compensating for any negative impacts of changes in the territory on the retention capacity of floodplains.

TITLE VIII
WATERWORKS

§ 55
Waterworks

(1) Waterworks are structures that serve for the impoundment and retention of water, the artificial regulation of the runoff regime of surface waters, for the protection and use of waters, for the management of waters, for protection against the harmful effects of waters, for the regulation of water conditions, or for other purposes pursued by this Act, in particular
a) dams, dikes, water reservoirs, weirs, and impoundments,
b) structures by which the beds of watercourses are regulated, changed, or established,
c) structures of water mains and waterworks facilities, including water treatment plants, sewer mains, sewer facilities, wastewater treatment plants, as well as structures for the treatment of wastewater before its discharge into a sewer system,
d) structures for flood protection,
e) structures for water management land improvements, irrigation, and land drainage,
f) structures established for navigation purposes in the beds of watercourses or on their banks,
g) structures for the utilization of water energy and energy potential,
h) tailings ponds,
i) structures serving for the observation of the status of surface or groundwaters,
j) wells,
k) structures for torrent and gully control, unless a special act²⁵) provides otherwise,
l) other structures necessary for the management of waters permitted under § 8.

(2) Water management modifications are earthworks and terrain modifications in the natural beds of watercourses and on adjacent lands, by which the natural beds of watercourses are substantially changed and which are necessary to ensure the functions of watercourses.

(3) For the purposes of this Act, simple facilities outside the bed of a watercourse on lands or structures for the collection of water and for their protection against the harmful effects of surface or groundwaters, water management modifications, land modifications, sealed tanks including the inflow pipeline, internal water supply systems, and internal sewer systems, exploratory hydrogeological wells, other facilities constructed as part of geological works⁸), and wells for utilizing the energy potential of groundwaters, if no pumping or abstraction of groundwater occurs, are not considered waterworks.

(4) In case of doubt as to whether it is a waterwork, the locally competent water authority shall decide.

§ 55a

Rights to lands and structures necessary for the implementation of public-benefit flood protection structures may be withdrawn or restricted according to the procedure under the Expropriation Act.

§ 56
Structures for Water Management Land Improvements

(1) For the purposes of this Act, structures for water management land improvements are considered to be structures
a) for the irrigation and drainage of lands,
b) for the protection of lands against water erosion.

(2) Structures for the drainage of agricultural lands are, for the purposes of this Act, divided into main drainage facilities and detailed drainage facilities, whereby a detailed drainage facility is understood for subsurface drainage as collector and main drains, drainage shafts and outlets, and for surface drainage as collector ditches and objects on them.

(3) The detailed definition of structures for water management land improvements and their parts, and the manner and scope of care for them shall be determined by the Ministry of Agriculture by decree.

(4) The owner of the land on which a structure for water management land improvements or its part is located, which is connected with more lands or was established in the public interest and was built before the effective date of this Act, is obliged to
a) tolerate the structure for water management land improvements or its part on their land,
b) use the land in such a way as not to negatively affect the function of the structure for water management land improvements or its parts,
c) report to the owner of the structure for water management land improvements, or to the water authority, apparent defects in the function of the structure or its part,
d) tolerate the use of their land to the necessary extent for the maintenance of the structure for water management land improvements or its part.

(5) The water authority is entitled, in case of doubt, to decide on the scope of the obligation of the owner of the lands on which the structure for water management land improvements or its part is located, the owners of lands adjacent to the land on which the structure for water management land improvements or its part is located, or possibly on the obligation of the administrator of the connecting watercourse to ensure the function of the structure for water management land improvements.

(6) The management of structures for water management land improvements that are the property of the state is carried out by the state through its organizational units, which the Ministry of Agriculture establishes for this purpose, unless the Ministry of Agriculture agrees on the management of these structures with legal persons to whom these structures serve or with whose activities they are related.

§ 57
Use of Waterworks by Other Persons

If another entitled person (§ 8) other than the owner of this waterwork has a direct benefit from the waterwork, they are obliged to contribute to the costs of maintaining this waterwork. If no agreement is reached between the owner of the waterwork and the entitled person on the amount and method of payment of the costs, a court shall decide. This does not apply if the owner of the waterwork is the administrator of the watercourse and the person entitled to manage waters under § 8 in this waterwork is obliged to pay the fee for the administration of watercourses and the administration of the river basin under § 101, and if the person entitled to manage waters under § 8 uses the water only for the purpose of utilizing its energy potential for electricity production in hydroelectric power plants with a total installed capacity of up to 10 MWe.

§ 58
Protection of Waterworks

(1) It is prohibited to damage waterworks and their functions.

(2) In particular, it is prohibited
a) to plant trees on protective dikes, to drive vehicles on them, unless it is for maintenance, except in designated places,
b) to damage water gauges, water meters, benchmarks, high water marks, and other facilities serving to fulfill the tasks set by this Act.

(3) The water authority may, at the proposal of the owner of a waterwork, in the interest of its protection, establish protection zones along it by a measure of a general nature and prohibit or restrict the location and implementation of certain structures or activities within them according to the nature of the waterwork. The owners of lands and structures in the protection zone are entitled to compensation from the owner of the waterwork for the property damage incurred by them due to the said prohibition or restriction. If no agreement is reached between the owner of the lands and structures in the protection zone and the owner of the waterwork on the amount of compensation, a court shall decide on its amount.

§ 59
Obligations of Waterwork Owners

(1) The owner of a waterwork is obliged to
a) comply with the conditions and obligations under which the waterwork was permitted and put into operation, in particular to comply with the operating rules and the approved manipulation rules, to immediately notify the water authority of changes affecting the content of the manipulation rules and to submit to the water authority for approval a proposal for an amendment to the manipulation rules so that it is in accordance with the complex manipulation plan under § 47 para. 4 let. g); the particulars of manipulation and operating rules shall be determined by the Ministry of Agriculture by decree,
b) maintain the waterwork in proper condition so as not to endanger the safety of persons, property, and other protected interests,
c) carry out technical safety supervision at their own expense for the waterwork, if the waterwork is subject to this supervision,
d) carry out, at their own expense, measures imposed on them by the water authority to remedy defects found on the waterwork, especially during water management supervision,
e) heed the instructions of the watercourse administrator in case of extraordinary situations on the affected watercourse,
f) remove objects and materials caught on or attached to the waterworks and to dispose of them according to a special act,³²)
g) install a benchmark, water mark, or water gauge on the waterwork, enable the continuous transmission of data on flows in the watercourse, or ensure a special modification of the spillway or outlet according to a decision of the water authority,
h) install navigation signs on the waterwork,
i) for a waterwork serving for the impoundment of water in a watercourse, to maintain at their own expense in proper condition the bottom and banks in the impoundment area and to care for the smooth flow of water therein, in particular to remove deposits and obstacles, and if it is technically possible and economically feasible, to create conditions for the migration of aquatic animals, unless it is a structure,
j) remove volunteer trees from dikes serving for flood protection, for the impoundment of water, or for the accumulation of water; the Act on Nature and Landscape Protection¹⁴a) does not apply to these obligations, with the exception of the protection of memorial trees, specially protected plant species, specially protected animal species, and free-living birds. Before their removal, unless there is a risk of delay, the owner of the waterwork is obliged to notify their intention to the nature protection authority,
k) carry out for the first time no later than 6 months after its commissioning and then once every two years, through a professionally competent person authorized by the Ministry of the Environment, a technical review of a waterwork notified under § 15a and to submit the results of these reviews to the water authority within 30 working days of the review. The owner of the waterwork is obliged to remedy the identified defects within 60 days of the review.

(2) An authorization to carry out a technical review of a waterwork notified under § 15a may be granted to a person who has a sufficient level of professional, technical, administrative, and organizational background and meets the prerequisites for a qualified performance of the review.

(3) The water authority may impose on the owner of a waterwork the obligation to prepare and submit to it for approval a manipulation plan for the waterwork; it may also set the conditions under which it issues the decision on approval, and a deadline for submitting or for the submitted manipulation plan, impose the obligation to supplement it or make other modifications. It may also impose a change to the approved manipulation plan of the waterwork and its submission for approval. The water authority approves the manipulation plan for a limited period.

(4) The owner of a waterwork notified under § 15a para. 3 shall prepare and submit a manipulation plan to the water authority for approval no later than with the application for a final use permit under the Building Act.
