(5) In exceptional cases, the water authority may impose or permit the owner of a waterwork an extraordinary manipulation on the waterwork beyond the scope of the approved manipulation plan. In such a case, the owner of the waterwork does not have an obligation to compensate the person entitled to manage waters in this work for not being able to manage waters in the maximum permitted quantity and with certain properties.

(6) If required by the public interest and if the person who is obliged to do so does not properly fulfill these obligations and has not remedied the situation within a set deadline, the water authority may decide that another person shall take over the operation or maintenance of the waterworks for a strictly necessary period. This operation and maintenance shall be provided by the designated person at the expense of the one who was obliged to fulfill these obligations; if there is no such person, these costs are borne by the state.

(7) The state participates in the removal of obstacles to the migration of aquatic animals in a watercourse caused by waterworks built before the effective date of this Act.

§ 59a
Obligation of Owners of Lands on which Waterworks are Located

The owner of a land is obliged to tolerate, for compensation, a waterwork built before 1 January 2002 on their land and its use.

§ 60
Entry to Lands

(1) The owners of lands adjacent to a waterwork are obliged, after prior consultation with them, to allow those who ensure the operation or carry out the maintenance of these waterworks to enter and pass over their lands to the necessary extent for the purpose of the operation and maintenance of the waterworks.

(2) If damage is caused to the landowner by entry to the land, they are entitled to its compensation.

§ 61
Technical Safety Supervision over Waterworks

(1) Technical safety supervision over waterworks (hereinafter "technical safety supervision") is understood as the assessment of the technical condition of a waterwork from the perspective of safety and stability and the possible causes of their failures. It is carried out in particular by observing and inspecting the waterwork, measuring its deformations, monitoring water seepage, as well as evaluating the results of all observations and measurements in relation to predetermined limit or critical values. Part of the technical safety supervision is also the preparation of proposals for measures to remedy identified deficiencies.

(2) Waterworks that serve for the impoundment and retention of water are subject to technical safety supervision. These are
a) dams, dikes, and weirs, with the exception of transverse structures in the beds of watercourses and adjacent areas whose height from the toe of the dam to the crest is less than 1 m and the total volume of impounded water does not exceed 1,000 m³, or fixed and immovable transverse impounding structures in the beds of watercourses whose fixed overflow crest is less than 1.5 m above the downstream riverbed,
b) structures for flood protection,
c) structures established for navigation purposes in the beds of watercourses or on their banks,
d) structures for the utilization of the energy potential of surface waters, with the exception of the transverse structures mentioned in letter a), and
e) other structures serving for the impoundment or retention of water, with the exception of reservoirs completely sunk into the ground without an impounding element, oxbow lakes, water mains and reservoirs, sewer networks, and recreational pools.

(3) Furthermore, the following structures are subject to technical safety supervision:
a) tailings ponds and
b) hydrotechnical adits and tunnels.

(4) From the perspective of technical safety supervision, waterworks are divided into categories I to IV according to the risk of endangering human lives, possible damage to property in the adjacent area, and losses from the restriction of functions and uses in the public interest.

(5) The criteria and procedure for the classification of waterworks into categories, the scope and frequency of carrying out technical safety supervision for individual categories of waterworks and in individual stages of their preparation, construction, modification of the completed waterwork, or operation, the particulars of preparing the scope of technical safety supervision measurements, the particulars of the technical safety supervision program, and the processing of the results of observations and measurements shall be determined by the Ministry of Agriculture by decree.

(6) The applicant for a permit for a new or modified completed waterwork is obliged to submit with the application for a permit an expert opinion for the classification of the waterwork into a category with a proposal of conditions for carrying out technical safety supervision, which is prepared by a person mentioned in paragraph 11. The expert opinion for the classification of the waterwork into a category contains the determination of the degree of safety of the waterwork during floods and a proposal and assessment of the parameters of safety and outlet facilities in accordance with special legal regulations⁶¹), ⁶²).

(7) The water authority shall decide on the obligation to ensure technical safety supervision on a waterwork, on its scope, possibly on the conditions of its implementation, and on the classification of the waterwork into category I to IV, taking into account the expert opinion under the preceding paragraph, usually within the framework of the permit for the construction or its modification. The regional authority may reserve the issuance of this decision for waterworks whose impact under paragraph 2 extends beyond the territory of the relevant water authority, and in the case of an impact under paragraph 2 extending beyond the territory of the region, the Ministry of Agriculture.

(8) If it is a waterwork under § 15a para. 3, subject to technical safety supervision, with the consent of the water authority to the notification, this waterwork is considered classified into category IV of technical safety supervision according to the expert opinion submitted with the notification. The scope, or possibly conditions, of technical safety supervision are considered determined by the consent of the water authority to the notification.

(9) The water authority may decide on a change in the category of a waterwork, the scope of technical safety supervision, or the conditions of its implementation, if the conditions under which the previous decision was issued have significantly changed.

(10) The Ministry of Agriculture manages the records of technical safety supervision, including the classification of waterworks into categories I to IV. The scope of data and the method of keeping the records of technical safety supervision shall be determined by the Ministry of Agriculture by decree.

(11) Technical safety supervision over waterworks of categories I to III, including the preparation of a technical safety supervision program and the preparation of the scope of technical safety supervision measurements, the preparation of expert opinions for the classification of waterworks into categories I to IV from the perspective of technical safety supervision may only be carried out by an authorized person within the scope of their authorization. If such a person is the owner of a waterwork of category I or II, they may not carry out technical safety supervision on it themselves nor prepare a technical safety supervision program for it.

(12) The authorized person is obliged to
a) ensure the continuous performance of technical safety supervision in the required scope and with the required personnel, even during floods, natural disasters, and crisis situations,
b) notify the Ministry of Agriculture of a transformation of the legal person and a change in the personnel, material, and technical equipment related to the performance of technical safety supervision, immediately after the realization of this change,
c) carry out technical safety supervision over waterworks in accordance with generally binding regulations and technical standards, especially from the perspective of their safety, stability, and possible causes of failure,
d) keep records of technical safety supervision of selected data on waterworks and on the performance of technical safety supervision for specified waterworks over which it performs technical safety supervision, to the extent and in the manner specified by a decree,
e) transmit data from the records of technical safety supervision kept by them under letter d) to the Ministry of Agriculture no later than the 15th day of the first month of the following quarter, to the extent and in the manner specified by a decree.

(13) The water authority is obliged to
a) keep records of technical safety supervision of selected data on waterworks and on the performance of technical safety supervision for waterworks of category IV, over which an authorized person does not perform technical safety supervision, to the extent and in the manner specified by a decree,
b) transmit data from the records of technical safety supervision kept by them under letter a) to the Ministry of Agriculture no later than the 15th day of the first month of the following quarter, to the extent and in the manner specified by a decree.

(14) An authorization for the performance of activities under paragraph 11, first sentence, may be granted only to a legal person who has the professional, personnel, and material equipment and meets the prerequisites for the qualified performance of these activities as determined by a decree. The particulars of the application shall be determined by the Ministry of Agriculture by decree.

(15) The Ministry of Agriculture may withdraw the authorization to carry out technical safety supervision if
a) the obligations specified in § 61 para. 12 are not fulfilled,
b) technical safety supervision has not been carried out continuously for at least 5 years over waterworks of category III,
c) technical safety supervision has not been carried out uninterruptedly over waterworks of categories I and II,
d) the preparation of expert opinions for the classification of waterworks into categories I to IV from the perspective of technical safety supervision has not been properly carried out,
e) the legal person has been transformed, or the legal person has entered into liquidation.

(16) The Ministry of Agriculture shall, by decree, determine the scope of selected data, the method of keeping the records of technical safety supervision, and the method of transmitting this data under paragraphs 12 and 13.

§ 62
Obligations of Owners and Builders of Waterworks during Technical Safety Supervision

(1) The owner, or possibly the builder, of a waterwork is obliged to ensure technical safety supervision at their own expense, to the extent determined by a decree of the Ministry of Agriculture under § 61 para. 5. The water authority may, by a decision, set further obligations for the implementation of this supervision.

(2) For waterworks classified into categories I to III, their owner, or possibly the builder, is obliged to ensure technical safety supervision through an authorized person and to participate in its implementation to the extent determined by a decree of the Ministry of Agriculture. For waterworks of category III, the owner or builder may carry out technical safety supervision themselves if they are an authorized person.

(3) For waterworks of category IV, the owner, or possibly the builder, may carry out technical safety supervision themselves.

(4) The owner, or possibly the builder, is obliged, for waterworks classified into categories I to III, to immediately notify the Ministry of Agriculture of the designation of an authorized person, or of its change. The same applies to waterworks of category IV, for which the owner, or possibly the builder, does not carry out technical safety supervision themselves, but through an authorized person.

(5) When carrying out technical safety supervision, the owner, or possibly the builder, of a waterwork classified into categories I to IV is obliged to
a) designate a natural person responsible for the performance of technical safety supervision and to notify their name, surname, residential address, or possibly workplace address, and telephone number to the relevant water authority; for waterworks of category IV, the owner of the waterwork is considered the person responsible for technical safety supervision, unless they have designated another person,
b) invite the relevant water authority to an inspection of the waterwork under § 61 para. 1, for structures of category I once a year, for structures of category II once every 2 years, for structures of category III once every 4 years, and for structures of category IV once every 10 years,
c) submit a record of the inspection of waterworks of categories I to IV within the deadlines under letter b) to the relevant water authority,
d) submit reports on the results of technical safety supervision for waterworks of categories I to III within the deadlines under letter b) or, if extraordinary circumstances affecting the safety of the waterwork have occurred, to the relevant water authority,
e) submit the technical safety supervision program or its amendment for waterworks of categories I to III to the relevant water authority.

TITLE IX
FLOOD PROTECTION

Division 1
Flood Protection

§ 63

(1) Flood protection means activities and measures to prevent and manage flood risk in a threatened area. It is ensured through systematic prevention and operational measures.

(2) Operational measures are ensured according to flood plans and, upon the declaration of a state of crisis, according to crisis plans.³⁴)

(3) To ensure flood protection, everyone is obliged to allow entry, or possibly passage, onto their lands, or possibly structures, to those who direct, coordinate, and carry out securing and rescue work, to contribute with personal and material assistance at the order of flood authorities to the protection of lives and property from floods, and to follow the orders of flood authorities.

(4) If damage is caused to the owner of the land or structure during this activity, they are entitled to its compensation.

§ 64
Floods

(1) For the purposes of this Act, floods are understood as a temporary significant increase in the water level of watercourses or other surface waters, during which water already floods the area outside the watercourse bed and may cause damage. A flood is also a state where water may cause damage by not being able to drain naturally from a certain area in a timely manner or its runoff is insufficient, or when an area is flooded by concentrated runoff of stormwater. A flood may be caused by natural phenomena, especially melting, rainfall, or the movement of ice (natural flood), or by other influences, especially a failure of a waterwork, which can lead to its collapse (breach) or an emergency solution to a critical situation on the waterwork (special flood).

(2) A flood begins with the declaration of the second or third degree of flood activity (§ 70) and ends with the revocation of the third degree of flood activity, unless the second degree of flood activity is declared at the time of the revocation of the third degree of flood activity. In that case, the flood ends with the revocation of the second degree of flood activity. A flood is also the situation described in paragraph 1, in which the second or third degree of flood activity was not declared, but the water level or flow in the relevant profile or precipitation reached a normative level for one of these degrees of flood activity according to the flood plan of the relevant territorial unit. In case of doubt as to whether a flood occurred in a certain area and at a certain time, the water authority shall decide, if any of these conditions are met.

(3) The danger of a flood is considered to be a situation, especially when
a) a specified limit of the water level or flow in a watercourse and its rising trend is reached,
b) prolonged heavy rainfall, or a forecast of the danger of intense rainfall, expected sudden melting, dangerous movement of ice, or the formation of dangerous ice jams and accumulations, or
c) an extraordinary situation arises on a waterwork, where there is a danger of its failure.

§ 64a
Flood Risk Management

(1) Flood risk management focuses on mitigating the potential adverse effects of floods on human health, the environment, cultural heritage, and economic activity, and, where considered appropriate, on non-structural measures or on reducing the probability of flooding.

(2) Flood risk is understood as the combination of the probability of a flood occurring and its potential adverse effects on human health, the environment, cultural heritage, and economic activity.

(3) A preliminary assessment of flood risks is the basis for defining areas with significant flood risk. For these areas, flood hazard maps, flood risk maps, and flood risk management plans are prepared or updated.

(4) Flood hazard maps define areas that could be flooded according to different flood scenarios and using established floodplains. Flood risk maps indicate the potential adverse consequences of floods according to these scenarios.

(5) Flood risk management plans are part of water planning and take into account important aspects such as costs and benefits, the extent and course of floods, the retention capacity of floodplains, water protection objectives under § 23a para. 1, land and water resource management, land-use planning, land use, nature protection, navigation, and port infrastructure. Flood risk management plans address all aspects of flood risk management, focusing on prevention, protection, and preparedness, including flood forecasts and early warning systems, and taking into account the characteristics of the specific river basin or sub-basin. Flood risk management plans may also include the promotion of sustainable land use, improvement of soil's water retention capacity, and controlled flooding of certain areas in the event of a flood.

Division 2
Flood Measures

§ 65
Flood Measures

(1) Flood measures are preparatory measures, measures taken during the danger of a flood, during a flood, and measures taken after a flood.

(2) Preparatory measures are
a) the establishment of floodplains,
b) the definition of normative limits for degrees of flood activity,
c) flood plans,
d) flood inspections,
e) preparation of the flood forecasting and warning service,
f) organizational and technical preparation,
g) the creation of material flood reserves,
h) preparation of flood protection participants.

(3) Measures during the danger of a flood and during a flood are
a) the activity of the flood forecasting service,
b) the activity of the flood warning service,
c) warning during the danger of a flood,
d) the establishment and activity of the patrol service,
e) the evacuation of floodplains,
f) the controlled influencing of runoff conditions,
g) flood securing works,
h) flood rescue works,
i) ensuring substitute functions and services in the area affected by the flood.

(4) Measures after a flood are
a) record-keeping and documentation work,
b) evaluation of the flood situation, including the resulting flood damages,
c) the removal of flood damages and the restoration of the area after a flood.

(5) Flood measures under paragraphs 1 to 4 do not include the construction, maintenance, and repair of structures and other facilities serving for flood protection, as well as investments induced by floods.

§ 66
Floodplains

(1) Floodplains are administratively designated areas that can be flooded by water during the occurrence of a natural flood. Their extent must be determined by the water authority at the proposal of the watercourse administrator. The water authority may impose on the watercourse administrator the obligation to prepare and submit such a proposal in accordance with the plans of the main river basins and the plans of the river basin districts.

(2) In built-up areas, in areas designated for development according to land-use planning documentation, or where necessary in other areas, the water authority shall, at the proposal of the watercourse administrator, define an active zone of the floodplain according to the danger of flood flows.

(3) The method and scope of preparing the proposal and determining floodplains and their documentation shall be determined by the Ministry of the Environment by decree.

(4) The water authority that has established a floodplain shall ensure that the documentation is made accessible and shall hand over one copy of this documentation to the Ministry of the Environment.

(5) If floodplains are not designated, the water and building authorities and land-use planning bodies may, in their activities, rely in particular on the available documents from river basin administrators and watercourse administrators on the probable boundary of the area threatened by floods.

(6) The Ministry of the Environment, based on the documents of the watercourse administrators, ensures the management of the documentation on established floodplains in the territory of the Czech Republic and ensures their registration in the public administration information system.

(7) Floodplains and their active zones are established by a measure of a general nature.

(8) When changing floodplains and their active zones, paragraphs 1 to 4 shall apply mutatis mutandis.

§ 67
Restrictions in Floodplains

(1) In the active zone of floodplains, it is prohibited to locate, permit, or construct structures, with the exception of waterworks by which the watercourse is regulated, flood flows are diverted, flood protection measures are carried out, or which are otherwise related to the watercourse or improve runoff conditions, structures for water collection, wastewater disposal, and stormwater drainage, and further necessary transport and technical infrastructure structures, the establishment of hop-growing structures, if they are established in a floodplain in cadastral areas defined under Act No. 97/1996 Coll., on the protection of hops, as amended, on the condition that such measures will be simultaneously taken that will minimize the impact on flood flows; this does not apply to the maintenance of structures and structural modifications, provided there is no deterioration of runoff conditions.

(2) In the active zone, it is also prohibited to
a) extract minerals and soil in a way that worsens the runoff of surface waters and carry out land modifications that worsen the runoff of surface waters,
b) store floatable material, substances, and objects,
c) erect fences, hedges, and other similar obstacles,
d) establish camps, campsites, and other temporary accommodation facilities; this does not apply to the establishment of camps consisting only of tents, which were established at this location before the establishment of the active zone of the floodplain and which can be immediately removed in case of flood danger.

(3) Outside the active zone in a floodplain, the water authority shall, according to the flood hazard or flood threat, by a measure of a general nature, establish restrictive conditions. When conditions change, it may change or abolish them by the same procedure. It shall proceed in this way also if the active zone is not established.

§ 68
Areas Designated for Controlled Flood Spills

(1) Areas designated for controlled flood spills are considered to be lands necessary for the impoundment, or possibly accumulation, of surface waters by public-benefit flood protection structures, for which the ownership right has been restricted by agreement or by the procedure under § 55a.

(2) For damage caused by a controlled flood spill to land, field crops, forest stands, and structures in the area under paragraph 1, the affected party is entitled to compensation, which is provided in money by the state, represented by the Ministry of Agriculture. The amount of compensation for damage caused to land or a structure is determined based on the amount of costs necessary to restore the land or structure to its original state, including the costs of removing undesirable deposits; the amount of compensation for damage caused to field crops is determined based on the market prices of the field crops at the time of the spill, including the costs of liquidating the damaged field crops; the amount of compensation for damage caused to forest stands is determined according to the Forest Act³³a). The procedure for determining and claiming compensation and the procedure for determining its amount shall be determined by the government by a regulation.

(3) Compensation is also due for financial loss incurred by the loss of entitlement to a subsidy provided under the Agriculture Act, which the affected party lost in connection with a controlled flood spill.

(4) The affected party to whom compensation has been provided under paragraph 2 cannot be provided with state aid on account of a flood spill under the Act on state aid for the restoration of a territory affected by a natural or other disaster.

(5) The affected party is not entitled to compensation if they do not comply with the conditions set for the use of lands designated for flood spills.

§ 69
Areas Threatened by Special Floods

Areas threatened by special floods are areas that can be flooded by water during the occurrence of a special flood. If the expected extent of an area threatened by a special flood for crisis situations significantly exceeds the floodplains, their extent shall be defined in the crisis plan. A special act applies to its preparation.³⁴)

§ 70
Degrees of Flood Activity

(1) Degrees of flood activity for the purposes of this Act are a measure of flood danger tied to normative limits, which are usually water levels or flows in reporting profiles on watercourses, or possibly limit or critical values of another phenomenon specified in the relevant flood plan.

(2) The scope of operational measures carried out for protection against a specific flood is governed by the danger or development of the flood situation, which is expressed by three degrees of flood activity, which are:
a) the first degree (state of vigilance) occurs at the danger of a natural flood and ceases when the causes of such danger have passed; this state also occurs upon the issuance of a warning information by the flood forecasting service; it requires increased attention to the watercourse or other source of flood danger, activates the warning and patrol service; on waterworks, this state occurs when the limit values of monitored phenomena and facts from the perspective of the work's safety are reached or when extraordinary circumstances are identified that could lead to the occurrence of a special flood,
b) the second degree (state of alert) is declared when the danger of a natural flood develops into a flood, but there are no major spills and damages outside the bed; it is also declared when the limit values of monitored phenomena and facts on a waterwork from the perspective of its safety are exceeded; flood authorities and other participants in flood protection are activated, means for securing works are put on alert, measures to mitigate the course of the flood are carried out according to the flood plan,
c) the third degree (state of danger) is declared in the immediate danger or occurrence of damages of a greater scope, the threat to lives and property in the floodplain; it is also declared when critical values of monitored phenomena and facts on a waterwork from the perspective of its safety are reached, simultaneously with the initiation of emergency measures; flood securing works are carried out according to the flood plans and, if necessary, rescue work or evacuation.

(3) The second and third degrees of flood activity are declared and revoked in their territorial district by the flood authorities. The basis is the achievement or the forecast of the achievement of the normative limit of levels or flows specified in the flood plans, a report from the flood forecasting or warning service, a recommendation from the watercourse administrator, a notification from the owner of a waterwork, or possibly other facts characterizing the degree of flood danger. The flood authority is obliged to inform the subjects specified in the flood plan and the higher flood authority of the declaration and revocation of flood activity.

(4) The normative limits of water levels for declaring the degrees of flood activity are contained in the flood plans and are binding for the flood plans of lower levels.

§ 71
Flood Plans

(1) Flood plans, for the purposes of this Act, are understood as documents that contain the method of ensuring timely and reliable information on the development of a flood, the possibilities of influencing the runoff regime, the organization and preparation of securing works; they also contain the method of ensuring the timely activation of flood authorities, securing the warning and patrol service and the protection of structures, the preparation and organization of rescue works, and ensuring the basic functions that have been disrupted by the flood in structures and in the area, and the established normative limits for the degrees of flood activity.

(2) The content of flood plans is divided into
a) a factual part, which includes data necessary for ensuring the protection against floods of a specific structure, municipality, river basin, or other territorial unit, normative limits for declaring the degrees of flood activity,
b) an organizational part, which contains lists of names, addresses, and the method of contacting the participants in flood protection, tasks for individual participants in flood protection, including the organization of the warning and patrol service,
c) a graphical part, which usually contains maps or plans on which floodplains, evacuation routes and assembly points, reporting profiles, and information points are marked.

(3) The flood plans of territorial units are
a) the flood plans of municipalities, which are prepared by the municipal authorities in whose territorial districts a flood may occur,
b) the flood plans of the administrative districts of municipalities with extended powers, which are prepared by the municipalities with extended powers,
c) the flood plans of the administrative districts of regions, which are prepared by the relevant regional authorities in their delegated capacity in cooperation with the river basin administrators,
d) the Flood Plan of the Czech Republic, which is prepared by the Ministry of the Environment.

(4) For structures threatened by floods, which are located in a floodplain or may worsen the course of a flood, their owners shall prepare flood plans for their own needs and for cooperation with the flood authority of the municipality. In case of doubt about the extent of this obligation or about which structures may worsen the course of a flood, the water authority shall decide.

(5) The water authority may impose an obligation to prepare a flood plan on the owners of lands that are located in floodplains, if it is necessary with regard to the manner of their use.

(6) The preparers of the flood plans of territorial units (paragraph 3) shall review their topicality annually, usually before the spring thaw period, and shall document this review. The preparers of other flood plans (paragraph 4) shall review them in case of substantial changes in the conditions under which they were prepared. If the review shows a need for amendment or supplementation of the flood plan, the preparers shall do so immediately.

(7) The factual and graphical parts of the flood plan of territorial units and their amendments are submitted by the preparers to the superior flood authority for confirmation of compliance with the flood plan of a higher level. For flood plans of lands and structures, compliance is confirmed by the flood authority of the municipality. If a structure significantly extends beyond the territory of the municipality in its scope or impact on the surroundings, the superior flood authority confirms the compliance and informs the lower flood authorities thereof. By confirming compliance, the factual and graphical parts of the flood plan become binding. The preparers shall continuously update the organizational part of the flood plan and provide it to the affected flood authorities and participants in the management of flood protection for use, if it is not accessible to them on the public administration portal in electronic form.

§ 72
Flood Inspections

(1) Flood inspections determine whether there are any defects on watercourses, waterworks, and in floodplains, or on objects or facilities located in these areas, that could increase the danger of a flood or its harmful consequences.

(2) Flood inspections are organized and carried out by flood authorities according to the flood plans, at least once a year.

(3) Flood authorities may, on the basis of a flood inspection, call upon the owners of lands, structures, and facilities in a floodplain to remove objects and facilities that may worsen runoff conditions or block the bed downstream. If these owners do not comply with the call within the specified deadline, such an obligation shall be imposed by a decision.

§ 73
Flood Forecasting and Warning Service

(1) The flood forecasting service informs the flood authorities, and where applicable, other participants in flood protection, about the danger of a flood occurring, about its occurrence and further dangerous development, about hydrometeorological elements characterizing the origin and development of a flood, especially about precipitation, water levels, and flows in selected profiles. This service is provided by the Czech Hydrometeorological Institute in cooperation with the river basin administrator.

(2) The flood warning service ensures information for flood authorities for warning the population in the place of an expected flood and in places located downstream on the watercourse, informs the flood authorities and participants in flood protection about the development of the flood situation, and transmits reports and messages necessary for its evaluation and for the management of flood protection measures. The flood warning service is organized by the flood authorities of municipalities and the flood authorities for the administrative districts of municipalities with extended powers, and other participants in flood protection participate in it. To ensure the flood warning service, the flood authorities of municipalities organize a patrol service if necessary.

(3) Owners of waterworks impounding water shall notify the relevant flood authorities, the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic, of the danger of a special flood and, in case of imminent danger, shall warn the immediately threatened natural and legal persons.

(4) The operational and information centers of the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic and the components of the integrated rescue system³⁵) are used for the transmission of information by the flood forecasting and warning service.

§ 74
Flood Rescue Works

(1) Flood rescue works are technical and organizational measures carried out during a flood in the immediately threatened or already flooded areas to save lives and property, especially the protection and evacuation of the population from these areas, their care for a strictly necessary period, the rescue of property and its relocation outside the threatened area.

(2) Flood rescue works in cases where human lives or economic interests, such as transport, supply, communications, and healthcare, are threatened, are ensured by the flood authorities in cooperation with the components of the integrated rescue system.

§ 75
Flood Securing Works

(1) Flood securing works are technical measures carried out during the danger of a flood and during a flood to mitigate the course of the flood and its harmful consequences.

(2) Flood securing works are in particular
a) the removal of obstacles in the watercourse and in the profile of objects (culverts, bridges) that prevent the smooth flow of water,
b) the breaking up of ice jams and accumulations in the watercourse,
c) the protection of the bed and banks against erosion by the flood flow and the securing of bank slides,
d) measures against the overtopping or breaching of protective dikes,
e) measures against the overtopping or breaching of the dikes of waterworks retaining water,
f) the temporary closing of breached dikes,
g) the installation of flood barriers,
h) measures against backwater, especially into sewer systems,
i) measures to limit water pollution,
j) measures ensuring the stability of the area against landslides.

(3) Flood securing works are ensured by the administrators of watercourses on the watercourses and by the owners of the affected objects, and where applicable, by other subjects according to the flood plans or at the order of the flood authorities. Securing works that may affect runoff conditions and the course of a flood must be coordinated in cooperation with the relevant river basin administrator for the entire watercourse or the entire river basin. Securing works carried out on waterworks classified into category I or II are discussed with the person authorized to carry out technical safety supervision (§ 61 para. 11), unless there is a risk of delay.

§ 76
Documentation and Evaluation of Floods

(1) The purpose of documentation is to ensure conclusive and objective records of the course of a flood, of the measures taken for flood protection, of the cause and extent of damages, and of other circumstances related to the flood. For this purpose, records in the flood log, continuous records of water levels and indicative values of velocities and flows, continuous records of data on the operation of waterworks affecting the course of a flood, marking of the highest reached water level, surveying and mapping of the inundation, monitoring of water quality and possible sources of pollution, photographic images and film recordings, purposeful field surveys, and investigations serve in particular.

(2) The flood authorities of municipalities and municipalities with extended powers and the participants in flood protection, who are obliged by law to do so, shall prepare a report on the flood during which flood activity was declared, flood damages occurred, or flood securing and rescue works were carried out. The flood authorities shall evaluate the flood, which includes an analysis of the causes and course of the flood, a description and assessment of the effectiveness of the measures taken, the material scope and an expert estimate of the amount of flood damages, and a proposal of measures to eliminate the consequences of the flood. They shall prepare the report within 3 months after the end of the flood; if more extensive documentation work is needed, a supplementary evaluation shall be carried out within six months after the end of the flood.

(3) The records of evaluated floods are ensured by the river basin administrators and, from a hydrological perspective, by the Czech Hydrometeorological Institute.

(4) Reports on a flood are submitted for use to the higher flood authority and for records to the river basin administrator.

Division 3
Flood Authorities

§ 77

(1) The management of flood protection is ensured by flood authorities. The management of flood protection includes preparation for flood situations, the direction, organization, and control of all relevant activities during a flood and in the period immediately following a flood, including the direction, organization, and control of the activities of other participants in flood protection. Flood authorities are guided by flood plans in their activities.

(2) In the period outside a flood, the flood authorities are
a) the authorities of municipalities and, in the capital city of Prague, the authorities of city districts,
b) the municipal offices of municipalities with extended powers and, in the capital city of Prague, the offices of city districts established by the Statute of the capital city of Prague,
c) the regional authorities,
d) the Ministry of the Environment; the preparation of rescue works is the responsibility of the Ministry of the Interior.³⁴)

(3) During a flood, the flood authorities are
a) the flood commissions of municipalities and, in the capital city of Prague, the flood commissions of city districts,
b) the flood commissions of municipalities with extended powers and, in the capital city of Prague, the flood commissions of city districts established by the Statute of the capital city of Prague,
c) the flood commissions of regions,
d) the Central Flood Commission.

(4) Flood authorities may, during a flood, take measures and issue operational orders to ensure flood protection, in justified cases even beyond the scope of the valid flood plans, provided that they immediately notify the affected persons. All measures taken and orders issued are recorded in the flood log and must be accessible for inspection by persons exercising the powers of the locally competent flood authorities, or in a manner enabling remote access. The Administrative Procedure Code does not apply to the issuance of these orders. The extraordinary powers of flood authorities begin with the declaration of the second or third degree of flood activity and end with the revocation of these degrees.

(5) Flood authorities or other persons on their order are entitled, during a flood, for the purpose of carrying out rescue and securing works, to enter foreign lands and objects to the necessary extent.

(6) State administration bodies and other bodies are obliged to assist flood authorities at their request in ensuring the management of flood protection.

(7) A flood authority of a lower level may request a flood authority of a higher level to take over the management of flood protection if it is unable to ensure this protection with its own forces.

(8) A flood authority that takes over the management of flood protection at the request of a flood authority of a lower level or on its own decision is obliged to notify the relevant lower flood authorities of the date and time of the takeover, the scope of cooperation, the termination of the management of flood protection, and to make a record of this in the flood log. The lower flood authorities remain active, carrying out measures in their territorial district according to their flood plans in coordination with the higher flood authority or according to its instructions.

(9) If a state of crisis is declared under another legal regulation³⁴), the relevant crisis staff and the relevant flood commission shall meet jointly. The powers of the flood authorities are not affected by the declaration of a state of crisis.

§ 78
Flood Authorities of Municipalities

(1) The municipal council may, to fulfill its tasks in flood protection, if there is a possibility of floods in their territorial districts, establish a flood commission; otherwise, this activity is ensured by the municipal council. The chairman of the municipal flood commission is the mayor. Other members of the commission are appointed from among the members of the municipal council and from natural and legal persons who are capable of carrying out measures or providing assistance in flood protection.

(2) The flood authorities of municipalities are subordinate to the flood authority of the municipality with extended powers.

(3) The flood authorities of municipalities, within their territorial districts, in ensuring the tasks of flood protection
a) confirm the compliance of the factual and graphical parts of the flood plans of the owners (users) of lands and structures, if they are located in a floodplain or worsen the course of a flood (§ 71 para. 4), with the municipal flood plan,
b) prepare the municipal flood plan and submit it for an expert opinion to the river basin administrator, and in the case of minor watercourses, to the administrator of these watercourses,
c) carry out flood inspections,
d) secure labor and material resources for carrying out rescue works and ensuring substitute functions in the area,
e) verify the preparedness of the protection participants according to the flood plans,
f) organize and ensure the flood warning service and patrol service, ensure the warning of legal and natural persons in the territorial district of the municipality using the unified warning system,
g) inform the flood authorities of neighboring municipalities and the flood authority of the municipality with extended powers about the danger and course of the flood,
h) declare and revoke the degrees of flood activity within their territorial competence,
i) organize, direct, coordinate, and impose measures for flood protection according to the flood plans and, if necessary, request personal and material assistance from authorities, legal and natural persons,
j) ensure evacuation and return, temporary accommodation and catering for evacuated citizens, ensure other rescue works,
k) ensure necessary hygienic and medical care during a flood, organize substitute supplies, transport, and other functions in the area disrupted by the flood,
l) carry out inspections after a flood, determine the extent and amount of flood damages, determine the effectiveness of the measures taken, and submit a report on the flood to the flood authority of the municipality with extended powers,
m) keep records in the flood log.

§ 79
Flood Authorities of Municipalities with Extended Powers

(1) The mayor of a municipality with extended powers establishes a flood commission of the municipality with extended powers and is its chairman. Other members of the commission are appointed from among the employees of the municipality with extended powers assigned to the municipal office and representatives of authorities and legal persons who are capable of carrying out measures or providing assistance in flood protection. In the case of concurrent activities of the flood commission of the municipality and the municipality with extended powers, the mayor entrusts the management of the municipal flood commission to another member of the commission. The flood authority of the municipality with extended powers is subordinate to the flood authority of the region.

(2) The flood authorities of municipalities with extended powers, within their territorial districts, in ensuring the tasks of flood protection
a) confirm the compliance of the factual and graphical parts of the flood plans submitted to them by the municipalities with the flood plan of the administrative district of the municipality with extended powers,
b) prepare the flood plan of the administrative district of the municipality with extended powers and submit it to the river basin administrator for an expert opinion,
c) organize the implementation of flood inspections,
d) verify the preparedness of the protection participants according to the flood plans,
e) organize professional training and exercises for the employees of the flood authorities of municipalities and the participants in flood protection,
f) impose on the owners of waterworks, as needed, modifications to the manipulation rules from the perspective of flood protection,
g) organize and manage the flood warning service in the territory of the administrative district of the municipality with extended powers, inform the flood authorities of neighboring municipalities with extended powers, the relevant river basin administrators, the Czech Hydrometeorological Institute, and the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic about the danger and course of the flood,
h) organize, direct, coordinate, and impose measures for flood protection according to the flood plans, direct and coordinate the measures carried out by the flood authorities of municipalities and, if necessary, request personal and material assistance from authorities, legal and natural persons,
i) declare and revoke the degrees of flood activity within their territorial competence,
j) use the operational center of the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic for the management of rescue works, for their coordination with the components of the integrated rescue system, and for communication with rescue work sites,
k) in necessary cases, if the regional flood commission is not convened, order, after agreement with the river basin administration, extraordinary manipulation on waterworks beyond the scope of the approved manipulation rules with a possible impact within the administrative district of the municipality with extended powers,
l) cooperate with the flood authorities of municipalities during a flood in ensuring hygienic and medical care, organize substitute supplies, transport, and other functions in the area disrupted by the flood,
m) collect reports on the extent and amount of flood damages, assess the effectiveness of the measures taken, and prepare a summary evaluation report on the flood,
n) keep records in the flood log.

§ 80
Flood Authorities of Regions

(1) The regional governor establishes the regional flood commission and is its chairman. The other members of the commission are appointed by its chairman from among the employees of the region assigned to the regional office, the relevant river basin administrators, and representatives of authorities and legal persons who are capable of carrying out measures or providing assistance in flood protection. The regional flood authority is subordinate to the central flood authority.

(2) The flood authorities of regions, within their territorial districts, in ensuring the tasks of flood protection
a) confirm the compliance of the factual and graphical parts of the flood plans submitted to them by the administrative districts of municipalities with extended powers with the flood plan of the administrative district of the region,
b) prepare the flood plan of the administrative district of the region according to § 71 para. 3 let. c) and submit it to the central flood authority,
c) verify the preparedness of the protection participants according to the flood plans,
d) impose on the owners of waterworks, as needed, modifications to the manipulation rules from the perspective of flood protection,
e) organize professional training and exercises for the members of the flood authorities of municipalities with extended powers and the participants in flood protection,
f) participate in the flood warning service in the territory of the region, inform the flood authorities of municipalities with extended powers, the Czech Hydrometeorological Institute, and the Ministry of the Environment about the danger and course of the flood,
g) organize, direct, and coordinate measures for flood protection according to the flood plans, direct and coordinate the measures carried out by the flood authorities of municipalities with extended powers,
h) declare and revoke the degrees of flood activity within their territorial competence,
i) direct, in their administrative district, the influencing of runoff conditions by manipulations on waterworks within the framework of the manipulation rules; order extraordinary manipulations on these waterworks beyond the scope of the approved manipulation plan after discussion with the affected flood authorities of municipalities with extended powers in their administrative district, with the relevant river basin administrators, and with the flood authorities of regions whose administrative districts may be affected by this extraordinary manipulation,
j) assess the impact of securing works on watercourses and waterworks on the runoff regime after discussion with the administrators of the watercourses and waterworks that may be affected by them, and coordinate their implementation,
k) prepare a summary evaluation report on the flood, including an analysis of the extent and amount of flood damages and the effectiveness of the measures taken,
l) keep records in the flood log,
m) use, for the management of rescue works, for their coordination with the components of the integrated rescue system, and for communication with rescue work sites, the relevant operational and information center of the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic.

§ 81
Central Flood Authority

(1) The Ministry of the Environment, as the central flood authority, within the framework of fulfilling its tasks in flood protection
a) directs flood protection and the exercise of supervision over it, with the exception of the management of flood rescue works, which is the responsibility of the Ministry of the Interior,
b) methodologically directs the preparation of measures for flood protection, especially the preparation, submission, and approval of flood plans, the organization of the flood forecasting and warning service,
c) prepares, after discussion with the relevant public administration bodies, the Flood Plan of the Czech Republic and submits it for approval to the Central Flood Commission,
d) confirms the compliance of the flood plans of the administrative districts of regions with the Flood Plan of the Czech Republic,
e) participates in the flood warning service, prepares expert documents for a possible takeover of the management of flood protection by the Central Flood Commission, provides information to the media,
f) ensures survey and documentation work of a larger scope (aerial observation, photography, etc.),
g) participates in the professional training of the staff of flood authorities.

(2) The Central Flood Commission is established by the government, which also approves its statute. The chairman of the Central Flood Commission is the Minister of the Environment, and the vice-chairman is the Minister of the Interior.

(3) The Central Flood Commission directs, controls, coordinates, and, if necessary, imposes in its full scope the management of flood protection during a flood threatening extensive areas, if the regional flood commissions are unable to take the necessary measures with their own forces and means. Within the framework of fulfilling its tasks in flood protection, it
a) informs the government about the course and consequences of floods,
b) orders, after discussion with the relevant regional flood authorities and the relevant river basin administrators, extraordinary manipulation on waterworks beyond the scope of the approved manipulation plan with a possible impact extending beyond the scope of the river basin districts under § 25 para. 2,
c) coordinates and controls the activities of the regional flood commissions,
d) keeps records in the flood log.

Division 4
Other Participants in Flood Protection

§ 82
River Basin Administrators

In addition to their duties as watercourse administrators, river basin administrators, in fulfilling their tasks in flood protection, shall
a) prepare expert opinions on the flood plans of the administrative districts of municipalities with extended powers,
b) cooperate in the preparation of the flood plans of the administrative districts of regions and the Flood Plan of the Czech Republic,
c) cooperate with the flood authorities of municipalities with extended powers in carrying out flood inspections,
d) provide initiatives to flood authorities for the imposition of necessary measures in floodplains, or other flood protection measures,
e) participate in the flood warning service, in particular by monitoring and evaluating the hydrological situation in the river basin and providing information to flood authorities, and cooperate with the Czech Hydrometeorological Institute in providing the flood forecasting service,
f) cooperate with the owners of waterworks in notifying the danger of a special flood,
g) propose to the flood authorities the declaration or revocation of degrees of flood activity,
h) provide professional, technical, and organizational support to the activities of regional flood commissions,
i) ensure the documentation of the course of the flood in the river basin,
j) after a flood, request reports from the flood authorities of municipalities with extended powers and from watercourse administrators, prepare a summary report for the river basin and submit it to the regional flood authorities and the Ministry of the Environment,
k) cooperate with the flood authorities of municipalities with extended powers and regions in the training and instruction of staff,
l) prepare proposals for organizational and technical improvements to flood protection and submit them to the flood authorities.

§ 83
Watercourse Administrators

Watercourse administrators, in fulfilling their tasks in flood protection, shall
a) prepare expert opinions on the flood plans of municipalities,
b) carry out flood inspections on watercourses in cooperation with the flood authorities of municipalities with extended powers,
c) propose to the relevant authorities that they impose on the owners of waterworks or other structures and lands on watercourses and in the floodplain the obligation to carry out necessary flood protection measures,
d) secure labor and material resources for carrying out the most essential securing works on watercourses,
e) during the danger of a flood, ensure the availability of their staff and the accessibility of material resources and verify their preparedness according to the flood plans,
f) monitor on the watercourses all phenomena relevant to the origin and course of a flood, especially the progress and extent of freezing, the formation of dangerous ice jams and accumulations, the progress of thawing and the movement of ice, water levels and flows, and where applicable, the accumulation of floating debris,
g) participate in the flood warning service, inform the flood authorities of municipalities with extended powers, the relevant river basin administrators, the office of the Czech Hydrometeorological Institute, and the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic about the danger and course of the flood,
h) provide professional assistance to the municipal flood commissions and the flood commissions of municipalities with extended powers,
i) propose to the flood authorities the declaration or revocation of degrees of flood activity,
j) carry out securing works on watercourses and take other measures according to the flood plans,
k) ensure the documentation of the course of the flood on watercourses,
l) after a flood, carry out inspections of the watercourse in cooperation with nature protection authorities and water authorities, determine the extent and amount of flood damages and draw up a protocol on them; they shall also assess the effectiveness of the measures taken and prepare a report on the flood and submit it to the flood authority of the municipality with extended powers, the relevant river basin administrator, and the office of the Czech Hydrometeorological Institute,
m) remove flood damages on the beds of watercourses, in particular by securing critical points in case of a future flood, and restore the flow capacity of the watercourse bed; special legal regulations do not apply to these activities;³⁴ᵃ⁾ the watercourse administrator shall notify the commencement of these activities 10 working days in advance to the relevant nature protection authority.

§ 84
Owners of Waterworks

(1) Owners of waterworks that may affect the course of a natural flood, in ensuring their tasks in flood protection, shall
a) carry out flood inspections of the waterworks in cooperation with the flood authorities of municipalities with extended powers and regions, in particular by checking the condition of the structures and their preparedness from the perspective of flood protection and remedying any identified defects,
b) secure labor and material resources for carrying out securing works on the waterworks,
c) during the danger of a flood, ensure the availability of their employees and the accessibility of material resources and verify their preparedness,
d) monitor on the waterworks all phenomena relevant to the safe passage of a flood, especially the function of the spillway structures, the progress and extent of freezing, the formation of dangerous ice jams and accumulations, the progress of thawing and the movement of ice, the water level, and where applicable, the accumulation of floating debris,
e) participate in the flood warning service, inform the flood authority of the municipality with extended powers, the watercourse administrator, the relevant river basin administrator, the office of the Czech Hydrometeorological Institute, and the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic about the danger and course of the flood,
f) operate the waterworks within the limits of the approved manipulation rules in such a way as to reduce the danger of flood damages; in doing so, they shall heed the instructions of the water management dispatcher of the relevant river basin administrator,
g) request the consent of the flood authority of the municipality with extended powers or the region for extraordinary manipulations on waterworks beyond the scope of the approved manipulation rules, according to the possible range of influence of the manipulation,
h) carry out securing works on the waterworks, including the impoundment area,
i) ensure the documentation of the course of the flood on the waterworks,
j) after a flood, carry out an inspection of the waterworks, determine the extent and amount of flood damages, assess the effectiveness of the measures taken, and provide the flood authority of the municipality with extended powers, the watercourse administrator, and the relevant river basin administrator with documents for the report on the flood,
k) remove flood damages on the waterworks, in particular by securing them for a potential future flood.

(2) Owners of waterworks of categories I to III (§ 61), who have been obliged to ensure the implementation of technical safety supervision, shall also
a) provide the relevant flood authorities, crisis management authorities,³⁴⁾ and bodies of the integrated rescue system³⁵⁾ with data on the parameters of a possible special flood (especially the characteristics of flood waves and the extent of the threatened area) and on the implementation of technical safety supervision (program) during a period of flood activity or crisis states; the water authority may set a deadline for fulfilling this obligation,
b) immediately notify the relevant flood authorities, watercourse administrators, and the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic of facts relevant to declaring states of alert and danger in the event of a special flood, if possible with a forecast of further development,
c) in the immediate threat to the safety of waterworks and a development leading to the disruption of their function and the occurrence of a special flood, warn the flood authorities downstream according to the flood plans of the territorial units, the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic, and in case of imminent danger, also the immediately threatened subjects.

(3) In the case of waterworks under construction, the builder shall fulfill the duties of the owner of the waterwork (paragraphs 1 and 2).

§ 85
Owners of Lands and Structures Located in a Floodplain or Worsening the Course of a Flood

(1) Owners of lands and structures located in a floodplain or worsening the course of a flood shall ensure that runoff conditions and the course of the flood are not worsened, in doing so they shall
a) prepare flood plans, if they have such an obligation under § 71 para. 4 or if it has been imposed on them by the water authority under § 71 para. 5,
b) carry out flood inspections in cooperation with the flood authorities, in particular by checking the condition of structures in the floodplain from the perspective of a possible impact on runoff conditions during a flood and the possible floating away of structures, their parts, and movable property,
c) at the order of the flood authority, remove their objects and facilities that may worsen runoff conditions or block the bed downstream,
d) secure labor and material resources for securing their objects and facilities that may worsen runoff conditions or block the bed downstream,
e) during the danger of a flood, ensure the availability of their staff and the accessibility of material resources and verify their preparedness according to the flood plan,
f) monitor all phenomena on the lands and structures relevant to the safe passage of a flood, especially the accumulation of floating debris and the blockage of the flow profile,
g) participate in the flood warning service, inform the flood authority, the watercourse administrator, and the Fire Rescue Service of the Czech Republic about the danger and course of the flood,
h) ensure the rescue of persons and their property, including a potential early harvest,
i) ensure the protection of vessels and facilities serving for navigation, if they are the owners or operators of a port; in doing so, they shall follow the instructions of the state navigation administration authorities,
j) carry out flood securing works, especially on culverts and bridges, road and railway embankments, so that their flow capacity is not limited,
k) after a flood, carry out an inspection of the lands and structures, determine the extent and amount of flood damages, and provide the flood authority with documents for the report on the flood,
l) remove flood damages, in particular by securing critical points in case of a future flood.

(2) In the case of structures under construction, the builder shall fulfill the duties of the owner of the structure.

(3) Owners of movable property in watercourses or in floodplains are obliged to ensure its placement and use in a manner that will not impede the runoff of high waters, or prevent the floating away of this property.

Division 5
Costs of Flood Protection Measures

§ 86

(1) Individual municipalities may take measures for the direct protection of property in their territory. The state and regions may contribute to these measures. Municipalities may request a contribution for their construction from the owners of the property protected by these measures.

(2) Legal and natural persons shall bear the costs they incur for their own measures to protect their property from floods.

(3) The costs of securing works on watercourses are borne by their administrators. The owners of waterworks shall bear the costs of securing works on these waterworks.

(4) The costs of rescue works, apart from the costs under paragraph 2, are borne by the municipalities, regions, and the state, in accordance with their powers in the flood protection system under a special legal regulation.³⁶)

§ 87
Property Damage Incurred as a Result of Activities or Measures Imposed during a Flood

Property damage incurred as a result of activities or measures imposed during a flood by
a) the municipal flood commission shall be compensated by the municipality,
b) the flood commission of the municipality with extended powers shall be compensated by the municipality with extended powers,
c) the regional flood commission shall be compensated by the region,
d) the Central Flood Commission shall be compensated by the Ministry of the Environment.

TITLE X
MANAGING DROUGHT AND WATER SCARCITY

Division 1
Definition of Terms

§ 87a

(1) For the purposes of this title, drought is understood as a hydrological drought, which is a variation in the hydrological cycle that arises mainly due to a deficit of precipitation and manifests itself in a decrease in flows in watercourses and groundwater levels.

(2) For the purposes of this title, a state of water scarcity is understood as a temporary state with a possible impact on basic human needs, economic activity, and the environment, where, as a result of drought, the demands for water use exceed the available water resources, and it is necessary to restrict water management and take other measures.

Division 2
Plan for Managing Drought and Water Scarcity

§ 87b

(1) A plan for managing drought and water scarcity (hereinafter the "drought plan") is prepared for the territory of the Czech Republic and for the territory of a region.

(2) The drought plan is a basis for
a) a decision or a measure of a general nature issued by the water authority under § 6 para. 4, § 59 para. 5, or § 109 para. 1 in managing a drought,
b) evaluating the necessity of convening a commission for managing drought and water scarcity (hereinafter the "drought commission"),
c) the decision-making of the drought commission on measures during a state of water scarcity.

(3) The drought plan includes
a) a basic part, which contains data necessary for managing drought in the given territory, characteristics of the territory, a description of water resources including backup and their possible substitution, a description of modifications, transport, transfers of water and water supply, a list and description of technical facilities usable for resolving a state of water scarcity, a list of water users significant for the given territory, a list of permitted water management activities significantly affecting water quantity and quality, a description of drought risks, and local normative limits and criteria for declaring a state of water scarcity,
b) an operational part, which contains a list of public authorities and persons participating in the management of drought and water scarcity, a description of the activities they perform, a description of information transfer, priorities of supply, a proposal of procedures for managing drought and measures during a declared state of water scarcity,
c) a graphical part, which contains maps or plans on which areas threatened by drought, water management and water supply systems, sources and water treatment plants, and water users significant for the given territory are marked.

(4) The determination of individual measures during a declared state of water scarcity in the drought plan must correspond to the significance of the water use. These methods of water use are determined progressively from the most significant to the less significant as follows:
a) ensuring the functionality of critical infrastructure according to regulations governing crisis management⁶³) and other operations providing essential services,
b) supplying the population with drinking water,
c) animal production, fish and aquatic animal farming, as agricultural production, and the ecological function of water,
d) economic use not falling under letters a) to c) and other use with a link to local employment,
e) other uses.

(5) If special local conditions so require, it is possible to deviate from the order of significance specified in paragraph 4 let. c) to e).

§ 87c

(1) The drought plan is prepared and continuously updated for the territory of a region by the regional authority, in cooperation with the relevant river basin administrators and the Czech Hydrometeorological Institute.

(2) The draft drought plan and its update shall be discussed by the regional authority with the municipal offices of municipalities with extended powers in its administrative district, the regional authorities of neighboring regions, the Police of the Czech Republic, the regional fire rescue service, the relevant district office, the regional hygienic station, water users significant for the territory of the relevant region, the Ministry of Agriculture, and the Ministry of the Environment. If a waterway of transport importance is located in the territory of the region, the regional authority shall also discuss the draft drought plan and its update with the Ministry of Transport and the State Navigation Administration. The drought plan and its update must not be in conflict with the drought plan for the territory of the Czech Republic and with the drought plans of other regions. The drought plan and its update, after approval by the Ministry of Agriculture and the Ministry of the Environment, shall be published by the regional authority in a manner enabling remote access.

§ 87d

(1) The drought plan for the territory of the Czech Republic is prepared and continuously updated jointly by the Ministry of Agriculture and the Ministry of the Environment.

(2) The draft drought plan and its update shall be discussed by the Ministry of Agriculture and the Ministry of the Environment with the regional authorities, river basin administrators, the Czech Hydrometeorological Institute, the Ministry of Transport, the Ministry of Health, and the Ministry of the Interior. The drought plan and its update shall be published by the Ministry of Agriculture and the Ministry of the Environment in a manner enabling remote access.

Division 3
Authorities for Managing Drought and Water Scarcity

§ 87e

(1) The authority for managing drought and water scarcity (hereinafter the "drought authority") is
a) the water authority under § 104 para. 2,
b) the central and regional drought commission.

(2) The superior administrative authority of the regional drought commission and the central drought commission is the Ministry of Agriculture or the Ministry of the Environment within the scope of the powers entrusted to them by this Act.

§ 87f

(1) The regional governor, as a special authority of the region, establishes a regional drought commission and is its chairman. The other members of this commission are appointed by the regional governor from among the employees of the region assigned to the regional office, the relevant river basin administrators, the Czech Hydrometeorological Institute, the Police of the Czech Republic, the regional fire rescue service, and the regional hygienic station. If a waterway of transport importance is located in the territory of the region, the regional governor shall also appoint an employee of the Ministry of Transport as a member of the regional drought commission.

(2) The regional governor shall invite the affected water users significant for the given territory, as listed in the drought plan, to the meeting of the regional drought commission and may invite in particular representatives of the affected municipalities. The invited persons are not members of the regional drought commission.

§ 87g

The central drought commission is established by the government. The central drought commission is chaired by the Minister of Agriculture or the Minister of the Environment.

§ 87h

If a state of crisis is declared under another legal regulation³⁴) during a state of water scarcity, the relevant crisis staff and the relevant drought commission shall meet jointly. The powers of the drought commissions are not affected by the declaration of a state of crisis.

Division 4
Drought Forecasting Service

§ 87i

The drought forecasting service informs the drought authorities about the danger of a drought occurring and about its further development. This service is provided by the Czech Hydrometeorological Institute in cooperation with the river basin administrators.

Division 5
Issuance of Measures during a State of Water Scarcity

§ 87j

(1) The regional authority, in cooperation with the river basin administrators, shall evaluate whether there is a threat of water scarcity in the entire territory of the region or its part, and shall propose to the regional governor the convening of the regional drought commission. The regional governor shall convene the regional drought commission, which shall evaluate whether it is necessary to declare a state of water scarcity. A state of water scarcity is declared and revoked by the regional drought commission; the provisions of § 25 paras. 2 and 3 of the Administrative Procedure Code shall apply mutatis mutandis. From the day of its posting on the official notice board of the regional authority, the state of water scarcity is considered declared or revoked.

(2) In the event that a state of water scarcity is declared, § 6 para. 4, § 59 para. 5, and § 109 para. 1 shall not be applied for the purpose of managing the drought.

(3) From the day of the enforceability or effectiveness of a measure of the regional drought commission under § 87k, the enforceability or effectiveness of a decision or a measure of a general nature issued by the water authority under § 6 para. 4, § 59 para. 5, and § 109 para. 1 in managing a drought is suspended to the extent specified therein, until the revocation of the state of water scarcity.

(4) From the day of the enforceability or effectiveness of a measure of the central drought commission under § 87k, the enforceability or effectiveness of measures issued during a state of water scarcity by a regional drought commission is suspended to the extent specified therein.

(5) The central drought commission shall be convened by the Minister of Agriculture or the Minister of the Environment, especially if requested by the chairman of a regional drought commission, or if a state of water scarcity has been declared in the territory of more than one region.

(6) The central drought commission directs and coordinates the individual measures of the regional drought commissions under § 87k, which in their impacts extend beyond the borders of regions, and, if necessary, issues measures under § 87k.

§ 87k

(1) A regional or central drought commission shall, during a state of water scarcity, issue measures for a strictly necessary period according to the nature of the matter by a decision or a measure of a general nature, in which it
a) regulates, restricts, or prohibits the general management of surface waters without compensation,
b) regulates, restricts, or prohibits permitted water management without compensation,
c) restricts the use of drinking water from a public water supply,
d) imposes on the owner of a waterwork an extraordinary manipulation on the waterwork beyond the scope of the approved manipulation plan,
e) orders the owner of a technical facility that serves for abstraction from a backup water source to put it into operation, if it is technically possible to use this backup water source,
f) adjusts the minimum residual flow or the minimum groundwater level set in a permit for the management of waters, or sets a minimum residual flow or a minimum groundwater level,
g) orders the owner of a necessary water management facility to put it into operation and to provide it for resolving the state of water scarcity, if it is technically possible, or
h) orders extraordinary monitoring of water quantity and quality.

(2) If a measure under paragraph 1 has the form of a decision, its issuance is the first act in the proceeding. An appeal does not have a suspensive effect.

(3) The regional drought commission shall immediately inform the superior administrative authority of its convening and of the measures issued under paragraph 1.

(4) The regional drought commission must act in accordance with the measures issued by the central drought commission.

(5) On the day of the revocation of a state of water scarcity, the measures issued by the relevant drought commission cease to be valid.

(6) The regional and central drought commissions shall keep a log of activities. In this log, the reasons for convening the drought commission, the reasons for declaring a state of water scarcity, the measures taken under paragraph 1, and the reasons for revoking the state of water scarcity are recorded.

(7) The necessary costs incurred for the implementation of measures under paragraph 1 let. e) and g) are borne by the region or the state according to the competence of the drought commission.

§ 87l
